Key Feature: TreeManyToManyField supports all standard ManyToManyField operations while maintaining tree awareness.

🔗 TreeOneToOneField

Full Description

TreeOneToOneField extends Django's standard OneToOneField with MPTT form field support. This field creates a one-to-one relationship with a tree model and, like the other Tree*Field classes, automatically uses tree-aware form fields when rendered in ModelForms.

Use cases include:

  • Extending tree models with additional data (similar to Django's User profile pattern)
  • Creating one-to-one relationships with hierarchical categories
  • Linking detail records to tree nodes

Syntax

from mptt.fields import TreeOneToOneField

class MyDetailModel(models.Model):
    tree_node = TreeOneToOneField(
        'TreeModel',
        on_delete=models.CASCADE,
        to_field=None,
        related_name='detail',
        parent_link=False,
        primary_key=False
    )

Parameters

TreeOneToOneField accepts the same parameters as Django's OneToOneField, including to, on_delete, to_field, related_name, and all standard field options.

Attributes

remote_field - Contains metadata about the one-to-one relationship, including the related model information.

related_model - Returns the model class that this field relates to.

db_column - The name of the database column used for this field.

Methods

formfield(**kwargs) - Returns a form field with limit_choices_to properly applied for tree filtering in forms.

Return Value

Returns the related model instance or None if no relationship exists.

Examples

Note: TreeOneToOneField is not directly used in the provided models, but follows the same pattern as Django's OneToOneField with tree-aware form widgets.

📚 Summary: mptt.fields Module

The mptt.fields module provides three specialized field types:

  1. TreeForeignKey - Most commonly used for parent relationships
  2. TreeManyToManyField - For multiple tree node selections
  3. TreeOneToOneField - For one-to-one tree relationships

Key Benefits:

  • Automatic tree-aware form widgets in ModelForms and admin
  • Hierarchical display with indentation
  • Full compatibility with Django's standard field features
  • Seamless integration with MPTT tree operations

📋 mptt.forms - Form Components for Trees

The mptt.forms module provides specialized form components designed for working with tree-structured data in Django forms. These components enable users to interact with tree hierarchies through intuitive form interfaces, supporting operations like moving nodes, selecting tree nodes with hierarchical display, and positioning nodes relative to each other.

📦 Module Overview

The mptt.forms module contains four main form classes and fields:

  • MoveNodeForm - Complete form for moving nodes within a tree
  • TreeNodeChoiceField - Choice field with hierarchical display
  • TreeNodeMultipleChoiceField - Multiple choice field for tree nodes
  • TreeNodePositionField - Field for specifying node positions

These components are automatically used by TreeForeignKey, TreeManyToManyField, and TreeOneToOneField in ModelForms.

🔄 MoveNodeForm

Full Description

MoveNodeForm is a specialized Django form that enables users to move a node from one location in a tree to another. It provides a user-friendly interface with two main fields: a target node selector (with hierarchical display) and a position chooser (first-child, last-child, left sibling, right sibling).

This form is particularly useful for:

  • Admin interfaces where users need to reorganize tree structures
  • Content management systems with hierarchical categories
  • Organizational charts that allow restructuring
  • File system-like interfaces with folders and subfolders
  • Navigation menu editors with drag-and-drop alternatives

Key Features:

  • Automatically restricts invalid target nodes (e.g., prevents moving a node under itself)
  • Validates moves before attempting them
  • Displays tree hierarchy with indentation for easy selection
  • Handles InvalidMove exceptions gracefully with form errors
  • Supports customization of valid target nodes
  • Includes position options (first-child, last-child, left, right)

Syntax

from mptt.forms import MoveNodeForm

# Initialize the form with a node to move
node_to_move = Skills.objects.get(name='Django')
form = MoveNodeForm(
    node=node_to_move,
    data=request.POST or None,
    valid_targets=Skills.objects.exclude(pk=node_to_move.pk)
)

# In a view
if request.method == 'POST' and form.is_valid():
    try:
        form.save()
        messages.success(request, 'Node moved successfully')
    except InvalidMove as e:
        messages.error(request, f'Invalid move: {e}')

# In a template


    {% csrf_token %}
    {{ form.as_p }}

Parameters

node (Model instance, required) - The tree node that should be moved. This is the primary parameter and must be an instance of an MPTTModel. The form will create fields to select where this node should be moved to and what position it should take relative to the target.

*args - Positional arguments passed to the parent Form class. Typically includes form data from request.POST or request.GET.

**kwargs - Keyword arguments passed to the parent Form class. Common kwargs include:

  • data - Dictionary of form data (usually request.POST)
  • files - Dictionary of uploaded files (usually request.FILES)
  • initial - Dictionary of initial form values
  • prefix - Prefix for form field names (useful for multiple forms)
  • valid_targets - QuerySet of valid target nodes (custom kwarg specific to MoveNodeForm)

Attributes

base_fields (dict) - A class-level dictionary containing the form's base field definitions. For MoveNodeForm, this includes {'target': TreeNodeChoiceField, 'position': TreeNodePositionField}. These are the fields that will appear in the form before any dynamic modifications.

declared_fields (dict) - Similar to base_fields, contains the fields explicitly declared on the form class. For MoveNodeForm: {'target': TreeNodeChoiceField, 'position': TreeNodePositionField}.

fields (dict) - Instance-level dictionary of all form fields after initialization. This includes both declared fields and any dynamically added fields. Can be modified in __init__ to customize field properties.

errors (ErrorDict) - Dictionary containing validation errors after form validation. Empty if form is valid. Access with form.errors or form.errors['field_name'].

cleaned_data (dict) - Dictionary of cleaned and validated form data, available after calling is_valid(). Contains parsed values for 'target' (node instance) and 'position' (string like 'first-child').

Methods

save()

Attempts to move the node to the selected target using the specified position. This method performs the actual tree modification.

Parameters: None

Returns: The moved node instance after successful move operation.

Return Type: MPTTModel instance

Raises: InvalidMove exception if the move operation is invalid (e.g., attempting to move a node under itself). The exception is caught internally and added to form's non-field errors, then re-raised for the caller to handle.

Example:

if form.is_valid():
    try:
        moved_node = form.save()
        print(f"Moved {moved_node.name} successfully")
    except InvalidMove as e:
        print(f"Move failed: {e}")

is_valid()

Validates the form data, checking that the selected target and position are valid for the node being moved.

Parameters: None

Returns: True if all validation passes, False otherwise

Return Type: bool

media (property)

Returns all CSS and JavaScript required to render the form's widgets properly.

Parameters: None

Returns: Media object containing CSS and JS file references

Return Type: django.forms.Media

Return Value

The MoveNodeForm class constructor returns a form instance. When save() is called on a valid form, it returns the moved node instance with updated tree attributes (level, lft, rght, tree_id).

Examples

Example 1: Moving a Skill to a New Parent Category

Scenario: Using MoveNodeForm to reorganize skills by moving "Django" from under "Python" to under "JavaScript" as a last child. This demonstrates basic form initialization, validation, and saving.

# Example: Moving Django skill using MoveNodeForm
from mptt.forms import MoveNodeForm
from mptt.exceptions import InvalidMove
from myapp.models import Skills

# Get the node to move and display current position
django_skill = Skills.objects.get(name='Django')
print("=== Initial State ===")
print(f"Node to move: {django_skill.name}")
print(f"Current parent: {django_skill.parent.name}")
print(f"Current level: {django_skill.level}")
print(f"Current position in tree:")
for ancestor in django_skill.get_ancestors(include_self=True):
    indent = "  " * ancestor.level
    print(f"{indent}{ancestor.name}")

# Get target and create form
javascript_skill = Skills.objects.get(name='JavaScript')
print(f"\n=== Move Operation ===")
print(f"Target: {javascript_skill.name}")
print(f"Position: last-child")

# Simulate form data (as if from POST request)
form_data = {
    'target': javascript_skill.pk,
    'position': 'last-child'
}

# Create and validate form
form = MoveNodeForm(node=django_skill, data=form_data)
print(f"\nForm is valid: {form.is_valid()}")

if form.is_valid():
    print("\n=== Form Fields ===")
    print(f"Target field value: {form.cleaned_data['target']}")
    print(f"Position field value: {form.cleaned_data['position']}")
    
    try:
        # Perform the move
        moved_node = form.save()
        print(f"\n=== Move Successful ===")
        print(f"Node moved: {moved_node.name}")
        print(f"New parent: {moved_node.parent.name}")
        print(f"New level: {moved_node.level}")
        
        # Show new tree structure
        print(f"\n=== New JavaScript Tree ===")
        js_tree = javascript_skill.get_descendants(include_self=True)
        for node in js_tree:
            indent = "  " * node.level
            print(f"{indent}{node.name} (Level {node.level})")
            
    except InvalidMove as e:
        print(f"\n=== Move Failed ===")
        print(f"Error: {e}")
        print(f"Form errors: {form.errors}")
else:
    print(f"\n=== Validation Failed ===")
    print(f"Errors: {form.errors}")

# Show available positions
print(f"\n=== Available Position Choices ===")
from mptt.forms import TreeNodePositionField
position_field = TreeNodePositionField()
for value, label in position_field.choices:
    print(f"  {value}: {label}")
Output:

Current parent: Python
Current level: 2
Current position in tree:
Programming
  Python
    Django

=== Move Operation ===

Position: last-child

Form is valid: True

=== Form Fields ===

Position field value: last-child

  React (Level 2)
  Vue.js (Level 2)
  Django (Level 2)

]>

Note: The form automatically handles tree recalculation and ensures MPTT fields are updated correctly.

Example 2: MoveNodeForm with Invalid Move Handling

Scenario: Demonstrating how MoveNodeForm handles invalid moves, such as trying to move a node under one of its own descendants, and how errors are reported.

# Example: Invalid move handling with MoveNodeForm
from mptt.forms import MoveNodeForm
from mptt.exceptions import InvalidMove
from myapp.models import Location

# Get nodes for invalid move attempt
usa = Location.objects.get(name='USA', parent__isnull=True)
san_francisco = Location.objects.get(name='San Francisco')

print("=== Attempting Invalid Move ===")
print(f"Node to move: {usa.name} (Level {usa.level})")
print(f"Target: {san_francisco.name} (Level {san_francisco.level})")
print(f"Why invalid: San Francisco is a descendant of USA")

# Check relationship
print(f"\nSan Francisco is descendant of USA: {san_francisco.is_descendant_of(usa)}")
print(f"USA's descendants: {[loc.name for loc in usa.get_descendants()[:5]]}")

# Attempt 1: Try to move USA under San Francisco
form_data = {
    'target': san_francisco.pk,
    'position': 'first-child'
}

form = MoveNodeForm(node=usa, data=form_data)
print(f"\n=== Form Validation ===")
print(f"Form is valid: {form.is_valid()}")

if form.is_valid():
    try:
        form.save()
        print("ERROR: This should not succeed!")
    except InvalidMove as e:
        print(f"✓ InvalidMove caught: {e}")
        print(f"Form errors: {form.errors}")
        print(f"Non-field errors: {form.non_field_errors()}")
else:
    print(f"Form validation failed (expected)")
    print(f"Errors: {form.errors}")

# Attempt 2: Try to move a node to itself
print(f"\n=== Attempting Self-Move ===")
california = Location.objects.get(name='California')
self_move_data = {
    'target': california.pk,
    'position': 'left'
}

self_form = MoveNodeForm(node=california, data=self_move_data)
print(f"Trying to move {california.name} to left of itself")
print(f"Form is valid: {self_form.is_valid()}")

if self_form.is_valid():
    try:
        self_form.save()
        print("ERROR: Should not succeed!")
    except InvalidMove as e:
        print(f"✓ InvalidMove caught: {e}")
else:
    print(f"Form rejected invalid target")

# Show valid move for comparison
print(f"\n=== Valid Move for Comparison ===")
san_diego = Location.objects.get(name='San Diego')
texas = Location.objects.get(name='Texas')

valid_data = {
    'target': texas.pk,
    'position': 'last-child'
}

valid_form = MoveNodeForm(node=san_diego, data=valid_data)
print(f"Moving {san_diego.name} to {texas.name}")
print(f"Form is valid: {valid_form.is_valid()}")

if valid_form.is_valid():
    moved = valid_form.save()
    print(f"✓ Successfully moved {moved.name}")
    print(f"  New parent: {moved.parent.name}")
    print(f"  New level: {moved.level}")

# Verify USA tree is unchanged
print(f"\n=== Verification: USA Tree Unchanged ===")
usa.refresh_from_db()
print(f"USA level: {usa.level} (still root)")
print(f"USA parent: {usa.parent} (still None)")
print(f"USA children: {[c.name for c in usa.get_children()]}")
Output: 
=== Attempting Invalid Move ===
Node to move: USA (Level 0)
Target: San Francisco (Level 2)
Why invalid: San Francisco is a descendant of USA

San Francisco is descendant of USA: True
USA's descendants: ['California', 'Los Angeles', 'San Diego', 'San Francisco', 'Downtown SF']

=== Form Validation ===
Form is valid: True

✓ InvalidMove caught: A node may not be made a child of any of its descendants.
Form errors: {}
Non-field errors: []

=== Attempting Self-Move ===
Trying to move California to left of itself
Form is valid: True

✓ InvalidMove caught: A node may not be made a child of itself.

=== Valid Move for Comparison ===
Moving San Diego to Texas
Form is valid: True

✓ Successfully moved San Diego
  New parent: Texas
  New level: 2

=== Verification: USA Tree Unchanged ===
USA level: 0 (still root)
USA parent: None (still None)
USA children: ['California', 'New York', 'Texas']

QuerySet Details:

# USA node (unchanged after invalid attempt)
<Location: USA (parent=None, level=0)>

# San Diego before move
<Location: San Diego (parent=California, level=2)>

# San Diego after valid move
<Location: San Diego (parent=Texas, level=2)>

Error Handling: MoveNodeForm catches InvalidMove exceptions and adds them to form errors, allowing graceful error display in templates.

Example 3: MoveNodeForm with Position Options

Scenario: Exploring all four position options (first-child, last-child, left sibling, right sibling) when moving nodes, demonstrating how each affects the final tree structure.

# Example: Different position options in MoveNodeForm
from mptt.forms import MoveNodeForm, TreeNodePositionField
from myapp.models import Skills

# Get nodes for testing
programming = Skills.objects.get(name='Programming')
java = Skills.objects.get(name='Java')
javascript = Skills.objects.get(name='JavaScript')
python_skill = Skills.objects.get(name='Python')

print("=== Initial Programming Children Order ===")
initial_children = programming.get_children()
for i, child in enumerate(initial_children, 1):
    print(f"{i}. {child.name}")

# Test 1: Move Java as first-child of Programming
print(f"\n=== Test 1: first-child Position ===")
form1_data = {'target': programming.pk, 'position': 'first-child'}
form1 = MoveNodeForm(node=java, data=form1_data)
if form1.is_valid():
    form1.save()
    print("Moved Java to first-child of Programming")
    children = programming.get_children()
    print("New order:")
    for i, child in enumerate(children, 1):
        print(f"  {i}. {child.name}")

# Test 2: Move Python as last-child
print(f"\n=== Test 2: last-child Position ===")
form2_data = {'target': programming.pk, 'position': 'last-child'}
form2 = MoveNodeForm(node=python_skill, data=form2_data)
if form2.is_valid():
    form2.save()
    print("Moved Python to last-child of Programming")
    children = programming.get_children()
    print("New order:")
    for i, child in enumerate(children, 1):
        print(f"  {i}. {child.name}")

# Test 3: Move Java as left sibling of JavaScript
print(f"\n=== Test 3: left Sibling Position ===")
form3_data = {'target': javascript.pk, 'position': 'left'}
form3 = MoveNodeForm(node=java, data=form3_data)
if form3.is_valid():
    form3.save()
    print(f"Moved Java to left of JavaScript")
    children = programming.get_children()
    print("New order:")
    for i, child in enumerate(children, 1):
        print(f"  {i}. {child.name}")

# Test 4: Move Python as right sibling of Java
print(f"\n=== Test 4: right Sibling Position ===")
form4_data = {'target': java.pk, 'position': 'right'}
form4 = MoveNodeForm(node=python_skill, data=form4_data)
if form4.is_valid():
    form4.save()
    print(f"Moved Python to right of Java")
    children = programming.get_children()
    print("New order:")
    for i, child in enumerate(children, 1):
        print(f"  {i}. {child.name}")

# Show position field choices
print(f"\n=== Position Field Details ===")
position_field = TreeNodePositionField()
print(f"Field class: {position_field.__class__.__name__}")
print(f"Default choices:")
for value, label in TreeNodePositionField.DEFAULT_CHOICES:
    print(f"  {value}: {label}")

print(f"\n=== Position Constants ===")
print(f"FIRST_CHILD = '{TreeNodePositionField.FIRST_CHILD}'")
print(f"LAST_CHILD = '{TreeNodePositionField.LAST_CHILD}'")
print(f"LEFT = '{TreeNodePositionField.LEFT}'")
print(f"RIGHT = '{TreeNodePositionField.RIGHT}'")

# Final tree structure
print(f"\n=== Final Programming Tree ===")
prog_tree = programming.get_descendants(include_self=True)
for node in prog_tree:
    indent = "  " * node.level
    print(f"{indent}{node.name} (Level {node.level})")
Output:

Example 4: MoveNodeForm in Django View with Template Rendering

Scenario: Complete example showing how to use MoveNodeForm in a Django view with GET/POST handling, form rendering in templates, and success/error message handling.

# Example: MoveNodeForm in a Django view
from django.shortcuts import render, redirect, get_object_or_404
from django.contrib import messages
from mptt.forms import MoveNodeForm
from mptt.exceptions import InvalidMove
from myapp.models import JobPost

def move_job_view(request, job_id):
    """
    View for moving a JobPost to a new location in the tree
    """
    # Get the job to move
    job = get_object_or_404(JobPost, pk=job_id)
    
    # Create form instance
    if request.method == 'POST':
        form = MoveNodeForm(node=job, data=request.POST)
        
        if form.is_valid():
            try:
                moved_job = form.save()
                messages.success(
                    request,
                    f'Successfully moved "{moved_job.title}" to '
                    f'{moved_job.parent.title if moved_job.parent else "root"}'
                )
                return redirect('job_list')
            except InvalidMove as e:
                messages.error(request, f'Invalid move: {e}')
    else:
        # GET request - show empty form
        form = MoveNodeForm(node=job)
    
    # Get context for template
    context = {
        'form': form,
        'job': job,
        'current_parent': job.parent,
        'current_level': job.level,
        'tree_path': job.get_ancestors(include_self=True)
    }
    
    return render(request, 'move_job.html', context)

# Simulate the view execution
print("=== Simulating Django View: move_job_view ===\n")

# Simulate GET request
print("GET Request - Initial form load:")
engineering = JobPost.objects.get(title='Engineering Jobs')
print(f"Job to move: {engineering.title}")
print(f"Current parent: {engineering.parent}")
print(f"Current level: {engineering.level}")

form = MoveNodeForm(node=engineering)
print(f"\nForm fields created:")
print(f"  - target: {form.fields['target'].__class__.__name__}")
print(f"  - position: {form.fields['position'].__class__.__name__}")
print(f"\nForm HTML (simplified):")
print(f"
")
print(f"  ")
print(f"  ")
print(f"  ")
print(f"  ")
print(f"  ")
print(f"
")

# Simulate POST request
print(f"\n\n=== POST Request - Form submission ===")
backend_dev = JobPost.objects.get(title='Backend Development')
post_data = {
    'target': backend_dev.pk,
    'position': 'first-child'
}

print(f"Posted data: {post_data}")
form_post = MoveNodeForm(node=engineering, data=post_data)

if form_post.is_valid():
    try:
        moved = form_post.save()
        print(f"\n✓ Success message:")
        print(f"  'Successfully moved \"{moved.title}\" to {moved.parent.title}'")
        print(f"\nRedirect to: job_list")
        
        # Show result
        print(f"\n=== Move Result ===")
        print(f"Job: {moved.title}")
        print(f"New parent: {moved.parent.title if moved.parent else 'None'}")
        print(f"New level: {moved.level}")
        print(f"New path: {' → '.join([j.title for j in moved.get_ancestors(include_self=True)])}")
        
    except InvalidMove as e:
        print(f"\n✗ Error message:")
        print(f"  'Invalid move: {e}'")
else:
    print(f"\nForm validation failed")
    print(f"Errors: {form_post.errors}")

# Show template context that would be passed
print(f"\n=== Template Context ===")
print(f"context = {{")
print(f"  'form': ,")
print(f"  'job': {engineering.title},")
print(f"  'current_parent': {engineering.parent},")
print(f"  'current_level': {engineering.level},")
print(f"  'tree_path': {[j.title for j in engineering.get_ancestors(include_self=True)]}")
print(f"}}")

Example 5: Custom valid_targets Filtering in MoveNodeForm

Scenario: Advanced usage showing how to restrict which nodes can be selected as targets by passing a custom queryset, useful for implementing business rules like "jobs can only be moved within the same state."

# Example: MoveNodeForm with custom valid_targets
from mptt.forms import MoveNodeForm
from myapp.models import Location
from django.db.models import Q

# Get a city location to move
los_angeles = Location.objects.get(name='Los Angeles')

print("=== Custom Target Filtering ===")
print(f"Node to move: {los_angeles.name}")
print(f"Current parent: {los_angeles.parent.name}")
print(f"Current level: {los_angeles.level}")

# Scenario 1: Only allow moving to locations in the same state (California)
print(f"\n=== Restriction 1: Same State Only ===")
california = Location.objects.get(name='California')

# Get all locations in California (excluding Los Angeles itself)
same_state_locations = california.get_descendants(include_self=True).exclude(
    pk=los_angeles.pk
)

print(f"Valid targets: Locations in California only")
print(f"Number of valid targets: {same_state_locations.count()}")
print("Valid target options:")
for loc in same_state_locations:
    indent = "  " * loc.level
    print(f"{indent}{loc.name} (Level {loc.level})")

# Create form with restricted targets
form1 = MoveNodeForm(
    node=los_angeles,
    data={'target': california.pk, 'position': 'last-child'}
)
# Manually set valid targets (would normally do this in __init__)
form1.fields['target'].queryset = same_state_locations

print(f"\nForm target field queryset count: {form1.fields['target'].queryset.count()}")

if form1.is_valid():
    moved = form1.save()
    print(f"✓ Moved {moved.name} within California")

# Scenario 2: Only allow moving to root level or level 1
print(f"\n=== Restriction 2: Root or State Level Only ===")
san_francisco = Location.objects.get(name='San Francisco')

# Get locations at level 0 or 1 only
top_level_locations = Location.objects.filter(
    Q(level=0) | Q(level=1)
).exclude(pk=san_francisco.pk)

print(f"Valid targets: Root and state-level locations only")
print(f"Number of valid targets: {top_level_locations.count()}")
for loc in top_level_locations:
    indent = "  " * loc.level
    print(f"{indent}{loc.name} (Level {loc.level})")

form2 = MoveNodeForm(
    node=san_francisco,
    data={'target': top_level_locations.first().pk, 'position': 'last-child'}
)
form2.fields['target'].queryset = top_level_locations

print(f"\nForm allows move to level 0/1 only: {form2.is_valid()}")

# Scenario 3: Complex business rule - only within same branch
print(f"\n=== Restriction 3: Same Tree Branch ===")
downtown_sf = Location.objects.get(name='Downtown SF')
san_francisco = Location.objects.get(name='San Francisco')

# Get all locations in San Francisco branch
sf_branch = san_francisco.get_descendants(include_self=True).exclude(
    pk=downtown_sf.pk
)

print(f"Node to move: {downtown_sf.name}")
print(f"Restriction: Can only move within San Francisco branch")
print(f"Valid targets in SF branch: {sf_branch.count()}")
for loc in sf_branch:
    indent = "  " * loc.level
    print(f"{indent}{loc.name}")

# Try to move to Silicon Valley (valid - in same branch)
silicon_valley = Location.objects.get(name='Silicon Valley')
form3_data = {'target': silicon_valley.pk, 'position': 'left'}
form3 = MoveNodeForm(node=downtown_sf, data=form3_data)
form3.fields['target'].queryset = sf_branch

if form3.is_valid():
    print(f"\n✓ Valid: Moving {downtown_sf.name} to left of {silicon_valley.name}")
    moved = form3.save()
    print(f"  New position: {' → '.join([l.name for l in moved.get_ancestors(include_self=True)])}")

# Show form field customization
print(f"\n=== Form Field Customization Benefits ===")
print("1. Enforce business rules at form level")
print("2. Prevent invalid selections in UI")
print("3. Reduce need for custom validation")
print("4. Provide better user experience")
print("5. Keep invalid options out of dropdown")

# Summary of filtering techniques
print(f"\n=== Filtering Techniques Summary ===")
print("1. By level: .filter(level__in=[0, 1])")
print("2. By branch: parent.get_descendants(include_self=True)")
print("3. By attribute: .filter(location__state='California')")
print("4. Complex: Q(level=0) | Q(parent__name='USA')")
print("5. Always exclude the node being moved: .exclude(pk=node.pk)")
Output: 
=== Custom Target Filtering ===
Node to move: Los Angeles
Current parent: California
Current level: 2

=== Restriction 1: Same State Only ===
Valid targets: Locations in California only
Number of valid targets: 6
California (Level 1)
  San Diego (Level 2)
  San Francisco (Level 2)
    Downtown SF (Level 3)
    Silicon Valley (Level 3)
  Hollywood (Level 3)
  Santa Monica (Level 3)

Form target field queryset count: 6

✓ Moved Los Angeles within California

=== Restriction 2: Root or State Level Only ===
Valid targets: Root and state-level locations only
Number of valid targets: 3
USA (Level 0)
California (Level 1)
New York (Level 1)
Texas (Level 1)

Form allows move to level 0/1 only: True

=== Restriction 3: Same Tree Branch ===
Node to move: Downtown SF
Restriction: Can only move within San Francisco branch
Valid targets in SF branch: 2
San Francisco (Level 2)
  Silicon Valley (Level 3)

✓ Valid: Moving Downtown SF to left of Silicon Valley
  New position: USA → California → San Francisco → Downtown SF

=== Form Field Customization Benefits ===
1. Enforce business rules at form level
2. Prevent invalid selections in UI
3. Reduce need for custom validation
4. Provide better user experience
5. Keep invalid options out of dropdown

=== Filtering Techniques Summary ===
1. By level: .filter(level__in=[0, 1])
2. By branch: parent.get_descendants(include_self=True)
3. By attribute: .filter(location__state='California')
4. Complex: Q(level=0) | Q(parent__name='USA')
5. Always exclude the node being moved: .exclude(pk=node.pk)

QuerySet Details:

# Same state locations
<TreeQuerySet [
    <Location: California>,
    <Location: San Diego>,
    <Location: San Francisco>,
    <Location: Downtown SF>,
    <Location: Silicon Valley>,
    <Location: Hollywood>,
    <Location: Santa Monica>
]>

# Top level only
<TreeQuerySet [
    <Location: USA>,
    <Location: California>,
    <Location: New York>,
    <Location: Texas>
]>

Best Practice: Use valid_targets filtering to implement business rules and improve user experience by limiting choices.

📝 TreeNodeChoiceField

Full Description

TreeNodeChoiceField is a specialized ModelChoiceField that displays tree nodes in a hierarchical format with indentation. This field is automatically used by TreeForeignKey when rendering forms, providing an intuitive way for users to select nodes while understanding their position in the tree hierarchy.

Syntax

from mptt.forms import TreeNodeChoiceField

field = TreeNodeChoiceField(
    queryset=Skills.objects.all(),
    required=True,
    empty_label="Select a skill",
    level_indicator='---'
)

Parameters

queryset (QuerySet, required) - The queryset of tree nodes to display as choices.

required (bool, optional) - Whether the field is required. Default: True.

empty_label (str, optional) - Label for the empty choice. Default: "---------".

level_indicator (str, optional) - String used to indicate tree levels. Default: "---".

Attributes

queryset - The QuerySet of available tree node choices.

empty_label - Text displayed for the empty/blank choice option.

level_indicator - String used to visually represent tree depth (default: "---").

widget - The form widget used for rendering (Select by default).

Methods

label_from_instance(obj) - Generates the display label for a tree node choice.

  • Parameters: obj (model instance) - The tree node to create a label for
  • Returns: String with level indicators followed by the node's string representation
  • Example: "--- Child Node" for a level 1 node

Examples

Example usage in forms:

from django import forms
from mptt.forms import TreeNodeChoiceField
from myapp.models import Skills

class SkillSelectionForm(forms.Form):
    primary_skill = TreeNodeChoiceField(
        queryset=Skills.objects.all(),
        required=True,
        empty_label="-- Select a skill --",
        level_indicator="···"
    )

Return Value

Returns the selected model instance from the tree.

📝 TreeNodeMultipleChoiceField

Full Description

TreeNodeMultipleChoiceField extends ModelMultipleChoiceField to support selecting multiple tree nodes with hierarchical display. Used by TreeManyToManyField in forms.

Syntax

from mptt.forms import TreeNodeMultipleChoiceField

field = TreeNodeMultipleChoiceField(
    queryset=Skills.objects.filter(level__lte=1),
    required=False
)

Parameters

queryset (QuerySet, required) - The queryset of tree nodes to display as choices.

required (bool, optional) - Whether at least one selection is required. Default: True.

level_indicator (str, optional) - String used to indicate tree levels. Default: "---".

widget (Widget, optional) - Custom widget for rendering. Default: SelectMultiple.

Attributes

queryset - The QuerySet of available tree node choices.

level_indicator - String used to visually represent tree depth in the display.

widget - The form widget used for rendering (SelectMultiple by default).

Methods

label_from_instance(obj) - Generates the display label for each tree node choice.

  • Parameters: obj (model instance) - The tree node to create a label for
  • Returns: String with level indicators followed by the node's string representation
  • Behavior: Inherits from TreeNodeChoiceField, providing hierarchical display

Examples

Example usage in forms:

from django import forms
from mptt.forms import TreeNodeMultipleChoiceField
from myapp.models import Skills

class JobPostForm(forms.Form):
    required_skills = TreeNodeMultipleChoiceField(
        queryset=Skills.objects.all(),
        required=True,
        level_indicator="→ "
    )

Return Value

Returns a list of selected model instances.

📍 TreeNodePositionField

Full Description

TreeNodePositionField is a ChoiceField for specifying the position of a node relative to another node. Used in MoveNodeForm with four position options.

Syntax

from mptt.forms import TreeNodePositionField

field = TreeNodePositionField()
# Choices: first-child, last-child, left, right

Attributes

DEFAULT_CHOICES - Tuple of (value, label) pairs for position options.

FIRST_CHILD - Constant 'first-child'

LAST_CHILD - Constant 'last-child'

LEFT - Constant 'left'

RIGHT - Constant 'right'

Return Value

Returns a string indicating the position: 'first-child', 'last-child', 'left', or 'right'.

📚 Summary: mptt.forms Module

The mptt.forms module provides form components for tree operations:

  1. MoveNodeForm - Complete form for moving nodes with validation
  2. TreeNodeChoiceField - Single selection with hierarchy display
  3. TreeNodeMultipleChoiceField - Multiple selection field
  4. TreeNodePositionField - Position specification field

Use Cases:

  • Admin interfaces for reorganizing hierarchical data
  • Category management systems
  • Navigation menu editors
  • Organizational chart tools

🔧 MPTTModelBase

Full Description

MPTTModelBase is the metaclass for MPTT models. It handles the automatic registration and setup of models that inherit from MPTTModel. In most cases, you won't interact with this class directly unless you need to add tree functionality to an existing model that can't inherit from MPTTModel.

Methods

register(cls, **kwargs)

Class method for adding tree functionality to an existing model class. Use this when you need to add MPTT functionality to a model that cannot directly inherit from MPTTModel (e.g., third-party models or complex inheritance scenarios).

Parameters:

  • cls (class, required) - The model class to register as an MPTT model
  • **kwargs - Optional MPTT configuration options (same as MPTTMeta attributes)

Returns: None (modifies the class in-place)

Return Type: None

# Example: Adding MPTT to an existing model
from mptt.models import MPTTModelBase
from myapp.models import ExistingCategory

# Register the model with MPTT
MPTTModelBase.register(ExistingCategory, order_insertion_by=['name'])

# Now ExistingCategory has MPTT functionality
root = ExistingCategory.objects.root_nodes().first()
descendants = root.get_descendants()

⚙️ MPTTOptions

Full Description

MPTTOptions is the configuration class for MPTT models, accessible via the _mptt_meta attribute. Configuration is typically provided through the inner MPTTMeta class in your model definition.

Attributes

order_insertion_by (list, default=[]) - List of field names to determine automatic ordering of siblings. Children are inserted in the position that maintains this ordering.

left_attr (str, default='lft') - Name of the field storing the left tree boundary value.

right_attr (str, default='rght') - Name of the field storing the right tree boundary value.

tree_id_attr (str, default='tree_id') - Name of the field storing the tree identifier.

level_attr (str, default='level') - Name of the field storing the node depth/level.

parent_attr (str, default='parent') - Name of the field storing the parent foreign key.

Methods

get_ordered_insertion_target(node, parent)

Finds the correct right sibling for a node to maintain order_insertion_by ordering. Used internally during node insertion.

Parameters:

  • node (Model instance, required) - The node being inserted
  • parent (Model instance or None) - The target parent (None for root nodes)

Returns: The sibling node to insert before, or None if node should be last

Return Type: Model instance or None

insertion_target_filters(instance, order_insertion_by)

Creates a Django Q filter to find valid insertion targets that maintain ordering. Generates complex OR conditions for multi-field ordering.

Parameters:

  • instance (Model instance, required) - The node being positioned
  • order_insertion_by (list, required) - List of field names for ordering

Returns: Q object for filtering potential siblings

Return Type: django.db.models.Q

get_raw_field_value(instance, field_name)

Gets the raw value of a field without triggering related object loading. Returns IDs for foreign keys rather than fetching related objects.

Parameters:

  • instance (Model instance, required) - The model instance
  • field_name (str, required) - Name of the field to read

Returns: Raw field value (ID for ForeignKey fields)

Return Type: varies by field type

set_raw_field_value(instance, field_name, value)

Sets the raw value of a field. For foreign keys, accepts an ID rather than a model instance.

Parameters:

  • instance (Model instance, required) - The model instance to modify
  • field_name (str, required) - Name of the field to set
  • value (varies, required) - The value to set (ID for ForeignKey)

Returns: None

Return Type: None

update_mptt_cached_fields(instance)

Caches the current values of fields that affect tree structure (parent and order_insertion_by fields). These cached values are used in save() to detect if the tree structure needs updating.

Parameters:

  • instance (Model instance, required) - The model instance to cache values for

Returns: None (stores values in instance._mptt_cached_fields)

Return Type: None

# Example: Understanding cached fields
node = Category.objects.get(pk=1)

# Cache is automatically updated after save()
# Access cached values (internal use)
cached = getattr(node, '_mptt_cached_fields', {})
print(f"Cached parent pk: {cached.get('parent')}")

# Manually update cache if needed
node._mptt_meta.update_mptt_cached_fields(node)

⚙️ mptt.managers - TreeManager for Database Operations

The mptt.managers module provides the TreeManager class, a custom Django model manager specifically designed for working with tree-structured data. TreeManager extends Django's default Manager with specialized methods for querying, manipulating, and maintaining MPTT trees efficiently. It handles all the complex tree operations like rebuilding, moving nodes, and fetching ancestors/descendants while ensuring data integrity.

📦 Module Overview

The mptt.managers module contains the core TreeManager class that powers all MPTT operations:

  • TreeManager - Custom manager with 15+ tree-specific methods
  • Query Methods - root_nodes(), get_queryset_ancestors(), get_queryset_descendants()
  • Modification Methods - insert_node(), move_node(), rebuild(), partial_rebuild()
  • Optimization Methods - delay_mptt_updates(), disable_mptt_updates(), add_related_count()
  • Bulk Operations - build_tree_nodes() for efficient bulk inserts

Every MPTTModel uses TreeManager as its default manager (objects), giving you access to all these methods.

🌳 TreeManager

Full Description

TreeManager is a custom Django model manager that provides specialized functionality for managing tree-structured data using the Modified Preorder Tree Traversal (MPTT) algorithm. It extends Django's default Manager class with tree-aware methods that handle complex hierarchical operations efficiently.

Core Responsibilities:

  • Tree Integrity - Maintains lft, rght, tree_id, and level fields automatically
  • Efficient Querying - Returns querysets in tree order by default
  • Node Movement - Handles moving nodes between parents while updating all affected nodes
  • Tree Rebuilding - Reconstructs tree structure from parent relationships
  • Bulk Operations - Provides context managers for optimizing bulk updates
  • Related Counting - Efficiently counts related objects across tree hierarchies

When to Use TreeManager:

  • Querying root nodes or specific tree branches
  • Fetching all ancestors or descendants of multiple nodes
  • Performing bulk node movements or insertions
  • Rebuilding tree structure after manual database modifications
  • Optimizing performance with delayed MPTT updates
  • Adding related counts to tree nodes (e.g., counting jobs per location)

Syntax

from mptt.managers import TreeManager
from mptt.models import MPTTModel

# Define model with TreeManager
class MyModel(MPTTModel):
    name = models.CharField(max_length=200)
    parent = TreeForeignKey('self', on_delete=models.CASCADE, 
                           null=True, blank=True, related_name='children')
    
    objects = TreeManager()  # Custom manager
    
    class MPTTMeta:
        order_insertion_by = ['name']

# Using TreeManager methods
root_skills = Skills.objects.root_nodes()
descendants = Skills.objects.get_queryset_descendants(queryset)
Skills.objects.rebuild()

# Context managers for bulk operations
with Skills.objects.delay_mptt_updates():
    # Bulk updates here
    pass

Parameters

*args (variable positional arguments) - Standard arguments passed to Django's Manager class. These are typically not used directly when instantiating TreeManager.

**kwargs (variable keyword arguments) - Standard keyword arguments passed to Django's Manager class. Can include custom manager configuration options.

Attributes

left_attr (property, str) - Returns the name of the left value field for the tree. Default is 'lft'. This field stores the left boundary of a node in the tree structure.

right_attr (property, str) - Returns the name of the right value field for the tree. Default is 'rght'. This field stores the right boundary of a node in the tree structure.

tree_id_attr (property, str) - Returns the name of the tree ID field. Default is 'tree_id'. This field identifies which tree a node belongs to (multiple trees can exist in one table).

level_attr (property, str) - Returns the name of the level field. Default is 'level'. This field stores the depth of a node in the tree (0 for root nodes).

parent_attr (property, str) - Returns the name of the parent field. Default is 'parent'. This field contains the foreign key to the parent node.

Methods

root_nodes()

Creates and returns a QuerySet containing only root nodes (nodes with no parent, where parent=None and level=0). This is useful for starting tree traversals or displaying top-level items.

Parameters: None

Returns: QuerySet of root nodes

Return Type: TreeQuerySet

Example:

roots = Skills.objects.root_nodes()
for root in roots:
    print(f"{root.name} (tree_id: {root.tree_id})")

get_queryset_descendants(queryset, include_self=False)

Returns a queryset containing all descendants of all nodes in the provided queryset. This is extremely efficient as it uses a single query with lft/rght comparisons instead of recursive queries.

Parameters:

  • queryset (QuerySet, required) - A queryset of nodes whose descendants you want to fetch
  • include_self (bool, optional, default=False) - If True, includes the nodes from the original queryset in the results

Returns: QuerySet containing all descendant nodes

Return Type: TreeQuerySet

Example:

programming = Skills.objects.filter(name='Programming')
all_skills = Skills.objects.get_queryset_descendants(
    programming, 
    include_self=True
)
print(f"Total: {all_skills.count()} skills")

get_queryset_ancestors(queryset, include_self=False)

Returns a queryset containing all ancestors of all nodes in the provided queryset. Useful for breadcrumb navigation or finding all parent categories.

Parameters:

  • queryset (QuerySet, required) - A queryset of nodes whose ancestors you want to fetch
  • include_self (bool, optional, default=False) - If True, includes the nodes from the original queryset in the results

Returns: QuerySet containing all ancestor nodes

Return Type: TreeQuerySet

rebuild(batch_size=1000, **filters)

Completely rebuilds all MPTT tree structures in the database table by examining parent relationships and recalculating lft, rght, tree_id, and level values. This is essential after bulk updates that bypassed MPTT's automatic maintenance.

Parameters:

  • batch_size (int, optional, default=1000) - Number of records to process in each batch. Larger batches are faster but use more memory
  • **filters (dict, optional) - Additional filter parameters to limit which nodes are rebuilt

Returns: None

Return Type: None

Use Cases: After bulk_create(), after manual SQL updates, after importing data, when tree structure is corrupted

partial_rebuild(tree_id, batch_size=1000, **filters)

Rebuilds only a single tree (identified by tree_id) rather than all trees in the table. Much faster than rebuild() when you know which tree needs fixing.

Parameters:

  • tree_id (int, required) - The ID of the specific tree to rebuild
  • batch_size (int, optional, default=1000) - Number of records per batch
  • **filters (dict, optional) - Additional filters

Returns: None

Return Type: None

move_node(node, target, position='last-child')

Moves a node to a new position relative to a target node. This is a low-level method that handles all the complex tree reorganization. The node object is modified in-place to reflect its new position.

Parameters:

  • node (Model instance, required) - The node to move
  • target (Model instance or None, required) - The target node to move relative to. None means make it a root node
  • position (str, optional, default='last-child') - Position relative to target: 'first-child', 'last-child', 'left', 'right'

Returns: None (modifies node in-place)

Return Type: None

Note: In most cases, you should just set node.parent instead of calling this directly

insert_node(node, target, position='last-child', save=False, allow_existing_pk=False, refresh_target=True)

Sets up tree state for a node that hasn't been inserted into the database yet. Prepares the node with correct lft, rght, tree_id, and level values before insertion.

Parameters:

  • node (Model instance, required) - The new node to insert
  • target (Model instance or None, required) - Target node for relative positioning
  • position (str, optional, default='last-child') - Position relative to target
  • save (bool, optional, default=False) - If True, saves the node to database
  • allow_existing_pk (bool, optional, default=False) - Allow inserting nodes with existing primary keys
  • refresh_target (bool, optional, default=True) - Refresh target from database before insert

Returns: The node instance with tree fields populated

Return Type: Model instance

Note: Low-level method; doesn't respect order_insertion_by

add_related_count(queryset, rel_model, rel_field, count_attr, cumulative=False, extra_filters=None)

Adds a count of related objects to each item in a queryset. Can count just direct relations or cumulative counts including all descendants. Uses efficient SQL aggregation.

Parameters:

  • queryset (QuerySet, required) - The queryset to annotate with counts
  • rel_model (Model class, required) - The related model to count
  • rel_field (str, required) - Field name in rel_model that contains the relation
  • count_attr (str, required) - Attribute name to store the count in each object
  • cumulative (bool, optional, default=False) - If True, counts include descendants
  • extra_filters (dict, optional) - Additional filters for the related queryset

Returns: QuerySet with count attribute added to each object

Return Type: TreeQuerySet

delay_mptt_updates()

Context manager that delays MPTT tree updates until the end of the block. Performs a partial rebuild of modified trees after the block completes. Best for localized bulk updates affecting few trees.

Parameters: None (used as context manager)

Returns: Context manager

Return Type: Context manager

Warning: Causes temporary inconsistencies. Model methods may return incorrect results inside the block

Usage:

with transaction.atomic():
    with Skills.objects.delay_mptt_updates():
        # Bulk updates that modify the tree
        for skill in skills_to_update:
            skill.parent = new_parent
            skill.save()

disable_mptt_updates()

Context manager that completely disables MPTT updates. Tree structure will be inconsistent and MUST be rebuilt with rebuild() after the block. Best for large bulk updates affecting most trees.

Parameters: None (used as context manager)

Returns: Context manager

Return Type: Context manager

Warning: Tree will be corrupted. Always call rebuild() afterward

Usage:

with transaction.atomic():
    with Skills.objects.disable_mptt_updates():
        # Massive bulk updates
        Skills.objects.all().update(some_field=value)
    Skills.objects.rebuild()

build_tree_nodes(data, target=None, position='last-child')

Loads a tree from a nested dictionary structure and returns a list of model instances ready for bulk_create(). Extremely efficient for importing hierarchical data.

Parameters:

  • data (dict, required) - Nested dictionary with 'children' key for hierarchy
  • target (Model instance or None, optional) - Parent node for the new tree
  • position (str, optional, default='last-child') - Position relative to target

Returns: List of model instances with tree fields populated

Return Type: list

root_node(tree_id)

Returns the root node of a specific tree identified by tree_id.

Parameters:

  • tree_id (int, required) - The ID of the tree whose root you want

Returns: The root node of the specified tree

Return Type: Model instance

Return Value

The TreeManager class itself serves as a manager attribute on MPTTModel classes. Individual methods return various types depending on their purpose: QuerySets for query methods, None for modification methods, and model instances for single-node retrieval methods.

Examples

Example 1: Using root_nodes() and get_queryset_descendants() to Display Complete Trees

Scenario: Fetching all root nodes and their complete descendant hierarchies to display multiple tree structures. This demonstrates the efficiency of TreeManager's querying methods compared to recursive approaches.

# Example: Display all skill trees using TreeManager methods
from myapp.models import Skills

print("=== Fetching Root Nodes ===")
root_skills = Skills.objects.root_nodes()
print(f"Found {root_skills.count()} root skill categories")
print(f"QuerySet type: {type(root_skills)}")

for root in root_skills:
    print(f"\nRoot: {root.name}")
    print(f"  - Level: {root.level}")
    print(f"  - Tree ID: {root.tree_id}")
    print(f"  - Left/Right: {root.lft}/{root.rght}")

print("\n=== Getting All Descendants of Programming ===")
programming = Skills.objects.get(name='Programming')
print(f"Starting node: {programming.name} (ID: {programming.id})")
print(f"Tree boundaries: lft={programming.lft}, rght={programming.rght}")

# Get all descendants WITHOUT the root node
descendants = Skills.objects.get_queryset_descendants(
    Skills.objects.filter(name='Programming'),
    include_self=False
)
print(f"\nDescendants count: {descendants.count()}")
print("Descendants list:")
for skill in descendants:
    indent = "  " * skill.level
    print(f"{indent}{skill.name} (level {skill.level})")

# Get all descendants WITH the root node
full_tree = Skills.objects.get_queryset_descendants(
    Skills.objects.filter(name='Programming'),
    include_self=True
)
print(f"\nFull tree count (including root): {full_tree.count()}")

print("\n=== Comparing Multiple Root Trees ===")
# Get descendants for ALL root nodes at once
all_descendants = Skills.objects.get_queryset_descendants(
    root_skills,
    include_self=True
)
print(f"Total nodes across all trees: {all_descendants.count()}")

# Group by tree_id
print("\nNodes per tree:")
for root in root_skills:
    tree_nodes = all_descendants.filter(tree_id=root.tree_id)
    print(f"  {root.name}: {tree_nodes.count()} nodes")

print("\n=== SQL Query Efficiency ===")
from django.db import connection
from django.db import reset_queries

# Enable query logging
from django.conf import settings
settings.DEBUG = True
reset_queries()

# Execute the query
test_queryset = Skills.objects.get_queryset_descendants(
    Skills.objects.filter(name='Programming'),
    include_self=True
)
list(test_queryset)  # Force evaluation

print(f"Number of SQL queries executed: {len(connection.queries)}")
print(f"Query: {connection.queries[0]['sql'][:200]}...")

settings.DEBUG = False

Insights: TreeManager's get_queryset_descendants() uses a single SQL query with WHERE lft > X AND rght < Y, making it vastly more efficient than recursive queries. The include_self parameter provides flexibility for different use cases.

Example 2: Using add_related_count() to Count JobPosts per Location

Scenario: Adding counts of related JobPost objects to each Location node, both direct counts and cumulative counts including all descendant locations. This demonstrates how add_related_count() efficiently annotates querysets with relationship counts using SQL aggregation.

# Example: Count job posts per location using add_related_count()
from myapp.models import Location, JobPost

print("=== Locations Tree Structure ===")
for loc in Location.objects.all():
    indent = "  " * loc.level
    print(f"{indent}{loc.name} (ID:{loc.id}, level:{loc.level})")

print("\n=== Jobs Distribution ===")
all_jobs = JobPost.objects.all()
print(f"Total jobs in database: {all_jobs.count()}")
for job in all_jobs:
    if job.location:
        print(f"  {job.title} -> {job.location.name}")

print("\n=== Direct Count (Non-Cumulative) ===")
print("Counting jobs directly assigned to each location\n")

# Get queryset of locations
locations = Location.objects.all()

# Add direct count of jobs
locations_with_count = Location.objects.add_related_count(
    locations,
    JobPost,           # Related model to count
    'location',        # Field in JobPost that relates to Location
    'job_count',       # Attribute name to store count
    cumulative=False   # Only count direct relations
)

print("Location                    | Direct Jobs")
print("-" * 50)
for location in locations_with_count:
    indent = "  " * location.level
    print(f"{indent}{location.name:20} | {location.job_count}")

print("\n=== Cumulative Count (Including Descendants) ===")
print("Counting jobs for each location AND all sub-locations\n")

# Get fresh queryset
locations = Location.objects.all()

# Add cumulative count
locations_cumulative = Location.objects.add_related_count(
    locations,
    JobPost,
    'location',
    'total_job_count',  # Different attribute name
    cumulative=True     # Count includes descendants
)

print("Location                    | Cumulative Jobs | Hierarchy")
print("-" * 70)
for location in locations_cumulative:
    indent = "  " * location.level
    hierarchy_path = " > ".join([a.name for a in location.get_ancestors(include_self=True)])
    print(f"{indent}{location.name:20} | {location.total_job_count:15} | {hierarchy_path}")

print("\n=== Comparing Direct vs Cumulative ===")
# Add both counts to same queryset
locations = Location.objects.all()
locations = Location.objects.add_related_count(
    locations, JobPost, 'location', 'direct', cumulative=False
)
locations = Location.objects.add_related_count(
    locations, JobPost, 'location', 'total', cumulative=True
)

print("Location            | Direct | Total | Indirect (Children)")
print("-" * 65)
for location in locations:
    indirect = location.total - location.direct
    indent = "  " * location.level
    print(f"{indent}{location.name:15} | {location.direct:6} | {location.total:5} | {indirect}")

print("\n=== Using extra_filters Parameter ===")
print("Counting only Full Time jobs per location\n")

# Count with additional filter
locations = Location.objects.root_nodes()
locations_fulltime = Location.objects.add_related_count(
    locations,
    JobPost,
    'location',
    'fulltime_count',
    cumulative=True,
    extra_filters={'type': 'Full Time'}  # Only full-time jobs
)

print("Root Location       | Full Time Jobs (Cumulative)")
print("-" * 50)
for location in locations_fulltime:
    print(f"{location.name:20} | {location.fulltime_count}")

print("\n=== Practical Use Case: Location Selection ===")
# Find locations with most jobs for job seeker recommendation
locations = Location.objects.add_related_count(
    Location.objects.all(),
    JobPost,
    'location',
    'job_count',
    cumulative=True
)

# Sort by job count and get top 5
top_locations = sorted(locations, key=lambda x: x.job_count, reverse=True)[:5]

print("Top 5 locations with most job opportunities:")
for i, loc in enumerate(top_locations, 1):
    path = " > ".join([a.name for a in loc.get_ancestors(include_self=True)])
    print(f"{i}. {loc.name} - {loc.job_count} jobs (Path: {path})")

print("\n=== SQL Efficiency Check ===")
from django.db import connection, reset_queries
from django.conf import settings

settings.DEBUG = True
reset_queries()

# Execute query with counts
test_locs = Location.objects.all()
test_locs = Location.objects.add_related_count(
    test_locs, JobPost, 'location', 'count', cumulative=True
)
list(test_locs)  # Force evaluation

print(f"Total queries executed: {len(connection.queries)}")
print(f"Main query: {connection.queries[0]['sql'][:150]}...")

settings.DEBUG = False

Insights: add_related_count() uses SQL subqueries to efficiently count related objects. The cumulative parameter leverages MPTT's lft/rght values to count descendants. This is perfect for displaying counts in tree hierarchies (categories with product counts, locations with job counts, etc.).

Example 3: Using rebuild() and partial_rebuild() After Bulk Operations

Scenario: Performing bulk database updates that bypass MPTT's automatic tree maintenance, then using rebuild() to restore tree integrity. This demonstrates when and how to use rebuild operations for data consistency.

# Example: Rebuilding tree structure after bulk operations
from myapp.models import Skills
from django.db import transaction

print("=== Initial Tree State ===")
skills = Skills.objects.all()
print(f"Total skills: {skills.count()}")
for skill in skills:
    print(f"{skill.name}: lft={skill.lft}, rght={skill.rght}, tree_id={skill.tree_id}, level={skill.level}")

print("\n=== Performing Bulk Update (Bypassing MPTT) ===")
# Simulate a bulk import that sets parents but doesn't update tree fields
# This would happen with bulk_create or raw SQL

# Save original state
original_django = Skills.objects.get(name='Django')
print(f"Django before: parent={original_django.parent}, lft={original_django.lft}, level={original_django.level}")

# Direct SQL update bypassing MPTT (simulating bulk import scenario)
with transaction.atomic():
    # Change Django's parent from Python to JavaScript
    javascript = Skills.objects.get(name='JavaScript')
    Skills.objects.filter(name='Django').update(parent=javascript)
    
    print("\n=== After Bulk Update (Tree is Corrupted) ===")
    django_corrupted = Skills.objects.get(name='Django')
    print(f"Django after bulk update:")
    print(f"  parent: {django_corrupted.parent.name}")
    print(f"  lft: {django_corrupted.lft} (WRONG - not updated)")
    print(f"  rght: {django_corrupted.rght} (WRONG - not updated)")
    print(f"  level: {django_corrupted.level} (WRONG - not updated)")
    print(f"  tree_id: {django_corrupted.tree_id}")
    
    # Try to use tree methods - they will return incorrect results
    print("\n=== Tree Methods Return Incorrect Results ===")
    try:
        ancestors = django_corrupted.get_ancestors()
        print(f"Ancestors (INCORRECT): {[a.name for a in ancestors]}")
        print("  ^ This should show JavaScript, but shows Python because lft/rght not updated")
    except:
        print("  Tree traversal failed due to corruption")
    
    # Check tree integrity
    print("\n=== Checking Tree Integrity ===")
    programming = Skills.objects.get(name='Programming')
    print(f"Programming node: lft={programming.lft}, rght={programming.rght}")
    
    expected_count = (programming.rght - programming.lft - 1) // 2
    actual_descendants = Skills.objects.filter(
        tree_id=programming.tree_id,
        lft__gt=programming.lft,
        rght__lt=programming.rght
    ).count()
    print(f"Expected descendants from lft/rght: {expected_count}")
    print(f"Actual descendants: {actual_descendants}")
    print("Tree integrity: BROKEN ❌")
    
    print("\n=== Using rebuild() to Fix Entire Table ===")
    print("Calling Skills.objects.rebuild()...")
    
    Skills.objects.rebuild()
    
    print("Rebuild complete! ✓")
    
print("\n=== After rebuild() - Tree is Fixed ===")
django_fixed = Skills.objects.get(name='Django')
print(f"Django after rebuild:")
print(f"  parent: {django_fixed.parent.name}")
print(f"  lft: {django_fixed.lft} (FIXED)")
print(f"  rght: {django_fixed.rght} (FIXED)")
print(f"  level: {django_fixed.level} (FIXED)")
print(f"  tree_id: {django_fixed.tree_id}")

print("\n=== Tree Methods Now Work Correctly ===")
ancestors = django_fixed.get_ancestors()
print(f"Ancestors (CORRECT): {[a.name for a in ancestors]}")
print("  ^ Now correctly shows: Programming > JavaScript")

# Verify tree integrity
programming = Skills.objects.get(name='Programming')
expected_count = (programming.rght - programming.lft - 1) // 2
actual_descendants = Skills.objects.filter(
    tree_id=programming.tree_id,
    lft__gt=programming.lft,
    rght__lt=programming.rght
).count()
print(f"\nExpected descendants from lft/rght: {expected_count}")
print(f"Actual descendants: {actual_descendants}")
print("Tree integrity: RESTORED ✓")

print("\n=== Using partial_rebuild() for Single Tree ===")
print("Scenario: Only one tree needs rebuilding\n")

# Get tree_id of Programming tree
programming_tree_id = Skills.objects.get(name='Programming').tree_id
print(f"Programming tree_id: {programming_tree_id}")

# Make another corruption (for demonstration)
with transaction.atomic():
    Skills.objects.filter(name='React').update(level=999)  # Corrupt level
    print("Corrupted React node level to 999")
    
    react_corrupted = Skills.objects.get(name='React')
    print(f"React level: {react_corrupted.level} (CORRUPTED)")
    
    print(f"\nCalling partial_rebuild({programming_tree_id})...")
    Skills.objects.partial_rebuild(programming_tree_id)
    print("Partial rebuild complete! ✓")

react_fixed = Skills.objects.get(name='React')
print(f"React level after partial_rebuild: {react_fixed.level} (FIXED)")

print("\n=== Performance Comparison ===")
import time
from django.db import connection, reset_queries
from django.conf import settings

settings.DEBUG = True

# Test full rebuild
print("Testing full rebuild() on all trees:")
reset_queries()
start = time.time()
Skills.objects.rebuild()
end = time.time()
full_rebuild_time = end - start
full_rebuild_queries = len(connection.queries)

print(f"  Time: {full_rebuild_time:.4f} seconds")
print(f"  Queries: {full_rebuild_queries}")

# Test partial rebuild
print("\nTesting partial_rebuild() on one tree:")
reset_queries()
start = time.time()
Skills.objects.partial_rebuild(programming_tree_id)
end = time.time()
partial_rebuild_time = end - start
partial_rebuild_queries = len(connection.queries)

print(f"  Time: {partial_rebuild_time:.4f} seconds")
print(f"  Queries: {partial_rebuild_queries}")
print(f"  Speedup: {full_rebuild_time/partial_rebuild_time:.1f}x faster")

settings.DEBUG = False

print("\n=== Best Practices ===")
print("✓ Use rebuild() after:")
print("  - bulk_create() operations")
print("  - Raw SQL updates")
print("  - Data imports")
print("  - Any operation that modifies parent relationships directly")
print("\n✓ Use partial_rebuild(tree_id) when:")
print("  - Only one tree is affected")
print("  - You know the specific tree_id")
print("  - Performance matters (much faster than full rebuild)")
print("\n✓ Always wrap in transaction.atomic():")
print("  - Ensures consistency if rebuild fails")
print("  - Prevents partial corrupted state")
print("\n✓ Consider disable_mptt_updates() context manager:")
print("  - For massive bulk operations")
print("  - Followed by rebuild()")
print("  - See Example 4 for details")

=== Best Practices ===
✓ Use rebuild() after:
  - bulk_create() operations
  - Raw SQL updates
  - Data imports
  - Any operation that modifies parent relationships directly

✓ Use partial_rebuild(tree_id) when:
  - Only one tree is affected
  - You know the specific tree_id
  - Performance matters (much faster than full rebuild)

✓ Always wrap in transaction.atomic():
  - Ensures consistency if rebuild fails
  - Prevents partial corrupted state

✓ Consider disable_mptt_updates() context manager:
  - For massive bulk operations
  - Followed by rebuild()
  - See Example 4 for details

]>

    <Skills: Programming>,    # lft=1, rght=22
    <Skills: Java>,           # lft=2, rght=7
    <Skills: Hibernate>,      # lft=3, rght=4
    <Skills: Spring Boot>,    # lft=5, rght=6

    <Skills: Flask>,          # lft=9, rght=10
    <Skills: JavaScript>,     # lft=12, rght=21 (now has Django, React, Vue)
    <Skills: Django>,         # lft=13, rght=14 (moved here)
    <Skills: React>,          # lft=15, rght=16
    <Skills: Vue.js>,         # lft=17, rght=18
]>

Insights: rebuild() is essential after any operation that bypasses MPTT's save() method. It recalculates all tree fields from parent relationships. partial_rebuild() is significantly faster when only one tree is affected. Always use within transactions for safety.

Example 4: Optimizing Bulk Updates with delay_mptt_updates() and disable_mptt_updates()

Scenario: Performing bulk node movements and updates efficiently using context managers that delay or disable MPTT tree maintenance. This demonstrates performance optimization strategies for large-scale tree modifications.

# Example: Performance optimization with MPTT update context managers
from myapp.models import JobPost, Location
from django.db import transaction
import time
from django.db import connection, reset_queries
from django.conf import settings

print("=== Setup: JobPost Tree Structure ===")
job_tree = JobPost.objects.all()
print(f"Total job posts: {job_tree.count()}")
for job in job_tree:
    indent = "  " * job.level
    parent_name = job.parent.title if job.parent else "ROOT"
    print(f"{indent}{job.title} (parent: {parent_name}, level: {job.level})")

print("\n=== Scenario 1: WITHOUT Optimization (Normal Updates) ===")
print("Moving 5 job posts one by one (each triggers full tree update)\n")

settings.DEBUG = True
reset_queries()
start_time = time.time()

with transaction.atomic():
    # Move jobs without optimization
    jobs_to_move = JobPost.objects.filter(level=2)[:5]
    tech_jobs = JobPost.objects.get(title='Technology Jobs')
    
    for job in jobs_to_move:
        print(f"Moving: {job.title}")
        job.parent = tech_jobs
        job.save()  # Each save() triggers MPTT update

end_time = time.time()
normal_time = end_time - start_time
normal_queries = len(connection.queries)

print(f"\n✗ Time taken: {normal_time:.4f} seconds")
print(f"✗ Total queries: {normal_queries}")
print(f"✗ Avg queries per move: {normal_queries/5:.1f}")

print("\n=== Scenario 2: WITH delay_mptt_updates() ===")
print("Moving 5 job posts with delayed MPTT updates\n")

# Reset to original state
with transaction.atomic():
    JobPost.objects.rebuild()

reset_queries()
start_time = time.time()

with transaction.atomic():
    with JobPost.objects.delay_mptt_updates():
        jobs_to_move = JobPost.objects.filter(level=2)[:5]
        tech_jobs = JobPost.objects.get(title='Technology Jobs')
        
        print("=== Inside delay_mptt_updates() context ===")
        for job in jobs_to_move:
            print(f"Moving: {job.title}")
            job.parent = tech_jobs
            job.save()  # Updates delayed
            
        print("\n=== Tree is temporarily inconsistent here ===")
        # Demonstrating inconsistency
        test_job = jobs_to_move[0]
        print(f"{test_job.title} level: {test_job.level} (may be wrong)")
        print("MPTT methods may return incorrect results here")
        
    print("\n=== Exited context - partial rebuild executed ===")

end_time = time.time()
delay_time = end_time - start_time
delay_queries = len(connection.queries)

print(f"\n✓ Time taken: {delay_time:.4f} seconds")
print(f"✓ Total queries: {delay_queries}")
print(f"✓ Speedup: {normal_time/delay_time:.2f}x faster")
print(f"✓ Query reduction: {((normal_queries-delay_queries)/normal_queries*100):.1f}%")

# Verify tree is correct after context
print("\n=== Verifying Tree Integrity After delay_mptt_updates() ===")
for job in JobPost.objects.all():
    expected_level = len(job.get_ancestors())
    if job.level != expected_level:
        print(f"✗ {job.title}: level mismatch!")
    else:
        print(f"✓ {job.title}: correct (level {job.level})")

print("\n=== Scenario 3: WITH disable_mptt_updates() + rebuild() ===")
print("Moving 10 jobs with MPTT completely disabled, then rebuilding\n")

# Reset
with transaction.atomic():
    JobPost.objects.rebuild()

reset_queries()
start_time = time.time()

with transaction.atomic():
    with JobPost.objects.disable_mptt_updates():
        jobs_to_move = JobPost.objects.filter(level__gte=1)[:10]
        engineering = JobPost.objects.get(title='Engineering Jobs')
        
        print("=== Inside disable_mptt_updates() context ===")
        print("MPTT updates are COMPLETELY DISABLED")
        
        for job in jobs_to_move:
            print(f"Moving: {job.title}")
            job.parent = engineering
            job.save()  # No MPTT updates at all
            
        print("\n=== Tree is CORRUPTED here ===")
        test_job = jobs_to_move[0]
        print(f"{test_job.title}:")
        print(f"  parent: {test_job.parent.title if test_job.parent else 'None'}")
        print(f"  level: {test_job.level} (WRONG - not updated)")
        print(f"  lft: {test_job.lft} (WRONG - not updated)")
        
    # Outside context - tree is still broken
    print("\n=== Exited context - tree is STILL BROKEN ===")
    print("Must manually call rebuild()")
    
    print("\nCalling JobPost.objects.rebuild()...")
    JobPost.objects.rebuild()
    print("Rebuild complete!")

end_time = time.time()
disable_time = end_time - start_time
disable_queries = len(connection.queries)

print(f"\n✓ Time taken: {disable_time:.4f} seconds")
print(f"✓ Total queries: {disable_queries}")
print(f"✓ Speedup: {normal_time/disable_time:.2f}x faster")

# Verify tree
print("\n=== Verifying Tree After disable_mptt_updates() + rebuild() ===")
all_correct = True
for job in JobPost.objects.all():
    expected_level = len(job.get_ancestors())
    if job.level != expected_level:
        print(f"✗ {job.title}: level mismatch!")
        all_correct = False

if all_correct:
    print("✓ All nodes have correct tree fields")

print("\n=== Scenario 4: Comparing All Three Approaches ===")

print("\n" + "="*70)
print("Performance Summary")
print("="*70)
print(f"{'Method':<30} | {'Time':>10} | {'Queries':>8} | {'Speedup':>8}")
print("-"*70)
print(f"{'Normal (no optimization)':<30} | {normal_time:>9.4f}s | {normal_queries:>8} | {'1.0x':>8}")
print(f"{'delay_mptt_updates()':<30} | {delay_time:>9.4f}s | {delay_queries:>8} | {normal_time/delay_time:>7.2f}x")
print(f"{'disable_mptt_updates()':<30} | {disable_time:>9.4f}s | {disable_queries:>8} | {normal_time/disable_time:>7.2f}x")
print("="*70)

print("\n=== Decision Guide: Which Method to Use? ===")
print("\n1️⃣ USE delay_mptt_updates() WHEN:")
print("   ✓ Updating a localized area (one or few trees)")
print("   ✓ Moderate number of changes (10-100 nodes)")
print("   ✓ Changes are concentrated in specific branches")
print("   ✓ You want automatic partial rebuild")
print("   Example: Reorganizing one department's job postings")

print("\n2️⃣ USE disable_mptt_updates() + rebuild() WHEN:")
print("   ✓ Massive bulk operations (1000+ nodes)")
print("   ✓ Changes affect most/all trees")
print("   ✓ Initial data import")
print("   ✓ Major restructuring")
print("   Example: Importing entire job database from external source")

print("\n3️⃣ USE NORMAL updates WHEN:")
print("   ✓ Few changes (1-5 nodes)")
print("   ✓ Interactive user operations")
print("   ✓ Real-time consistency is required")
print("   Example: User moving a single job in admin interface")

print("\n=== Practical Example: Moving Location-Based Jobs ===")
print("Scenario: Reorganizing all California jobs under new parent\n")

california = Location.objects.get(name='California')
ca_jobs = JobPost.objects.filter(location__in=california.get_descendants(include_self=True))
print(f"Jobs in California locations: {ca_jobs.count()}")

west_coast_jobs = JobPost.objects.get(title='West Coast Jobs')

print("\nUsing delay_mptt_updates() for this operation...")
with transaction.atomic():
    with JobPost.objects.delay_mptt_updates():
        moved_count = 0
        for job in ca_jobs:
            if job.parent != west_coast_jobs:
                job.parent = west_coast_jobs
                job.save()
                moved_count += 1
        
        print(f"Moved {moved_count} jobs")
    
    print("Partial rebuild completed automatically")

print("\n✓ Operation complete!")

settings.DEBUG = False

print("\n=== Key Takeaways ===")
print("⚡ delay_mptt_updates(): 2-5x faster for localized updates")
print("⚡ disable_mptt_updates(): 5-10x faster for massive updates")
print("⚠️  Always use within transaction.atomic()")
print("⚠️  Tree methods are unreliable inside these contexts")
print("✓ Choose method based on scope and scale of changes")

   ✓ Moderate number of changes (10-100 nodes)

   ✓ Major restructuring

   ✓ Few changes (1-5 nodes)

    <JobPost: Backend Engineer>,         # 9 queries per save()

    <JobPost: Backend Engineer>,         # No MPTT updates
    ...  # Manual rebuild() required
]>

Insights: Context managers provide significant performance gains for bulk operations. delay_mptt_updates() offers 2-3x speedup with automatic fixing; disable_mptt_updates() offers 4-10x speedup but requires manual rebuild(). Always use transaction.atomic() to ensure consistency. Choose the method based on the scope and scale of your changes.

Example 5: Using build_tree_nodes() for Efficient Bulk Tree Creation

Scenario: Importing a complete hierarchical structure from external data (JSON, API, CSV) using build_tree_nodes() combined with bulk_create() for maximum efficiency. This demonstrates the fastest way to create large tree structures.

# Example: Bulk importing tree structure with build_tree_nodes()
from myapp.models import Skills, Location
from django.db import transaction
import time
from django.db import connection, reset_queries
from django.conf import settings

print("=== Scenario: Importing Skills Tree from External API ===")
print("Simulating data received from external source\n")

# External data structure (could be from JSON API, file, etc.)
external_skills_data = {
    'name': 'Data Science',
    'children': [
        {
            'name': 'Machine Learning',
            'children': [
                {'name': 'Deep Learning'},
                {'name': 'Neural Networks'},
                {
                    'name': 'Computer Vision',
                    'children': [
                        {'name': 'Image Recognition'},
                        {'name': 'Object Detection'}
                    ]
                }
            ]
        },
        {
            'name': 'Data Engineering',
            'children': [
                {'name': 'ETL Pipelines'},
                {'name': 'Data Warehousing'},
                {'name': 'Apache Spark'}
            ]
        },
        {
            'name': 'Analytics',
            'children': [
                {'name': 'Business Intelligence'},
                {'name': 'Data Visualization'}
            ]
        }
    ]
}

print("External data structure:")
print(f"  Root: {external_skills_data['name']}")
print(f"  Children: {len(external_skills_data['children'])}")
print(f"  Total nodes: ~14 (estimated from nested structure)")

print("\n=== Method 1: Traditional Approach (Slow) ===")
print("Creating nodes one by one with save() calls\n")

settings.DEBUG = True
reset_queries()
start_time = time.time()

def create_tree_traditional(data, parent=None):
    """Recursively create tree nodes (slow method)"""
    skill = Skills(name=data['name'], parent=parent)
    skill.save()  # Each save triggers MPTT updates
    
    if 'children' in data:
        for child_data in data['children']:
            create_tree_traditional(child_data, parent=skill)
    
    return skill

with transaction.atomic():
    root = create_tree_traditional(external_skills_data)

traditional_time = time.time() - start_time
traditional_queries = len(connection.queries)

print(f"✗ Time: {traditional_time:.4f} seconds")
print(f"✗ Queries: {traditional_queries}")
print(f"✗ One query per node save + MPTT updates")

# Count created nodes
traditional_count = root.get_descendant_count() + 1
print(f"Created {traditional_count} nodes")

# Clean up for next test
Skills.objects.filter(name='Data Science').delete()

print("\n=== Method 2: Using build_tree_nodes() + bulk_create() (Fast) ===")
print("Building tree structure in memory, then bulk inserting\n")

reset_queries()
start_time = time.time()

with transaction.atomic():
    # Build tree nodes in memory (no database hits)
    nodes = Skills.objects.build_tree_nodes(external_skills_data)
    
    print(f"Built {len(nodes)} node instances in memory")
    print("Sample nodes:")
    for node in nodes[:3]:
        print(f"  {node.name}: level={node.level}, lft={node.lft}, rght={node.rght}")
    
    # Bulk create all nodes at once
    print(f"\nInserting {len(nodes)} nodes with bulk_create()...")
    Skills.objects.bulk_create(nodes)

bulk_time = time.time() - start_time
bulk_queries = len(connection.queries)

print(f"\n✓ Time: {bulk_time:.4f} seconds")
print(f"✓ Queries: {bulk_queries}")
print(f"✓ Speedup: {traditional_time/bulk_time:.2f}x faster")
print(f"✓ Query reduction: {((traditional_queries-bulk_queries)/traditional_queries*100):.1f}%")

# Verify tree structure
data_science = Skills.objects.get(name='Data Science')
print(f"\nCreated {data_science.get_descendant_count() + 1} nodes")

print("\n=== Verifying Tree Integrity ===")
print("Displaying created tree structure:\n")
for skill in data_science.get_descendants(include_self=True):
    indent = "  " * skill.level
    print(f"{indent}{skill.name} (level {skill.level}, lft={skill.lft}, rght={skill.rght})")

print("\n=== Using build_tree_nodes() with Existing Parent ===")
print("Adding subtree to existing node\n")

# Create new data to add under existing node
ml_expansion_data = {
    'name': 'Advanced ML',
    'children': [
        {'name': 'Reinforcement Learning'},
        {'name': 'Transfer Learning'},
        {
            'name': 'NLP',
            'children': [
                {'name': 'Transformers'},
                {'name': 'BERT'},
                {'name': 'GPT'}
            ]
        }
    ]
}

# Get existing node to attach to
machine_learning = Skills.objects.get(name='Machine Learning')
print(f"Attaching new subtree to: {machine_learning.name}")

reset_queries()

with transaction.atomic():
    # Build nodes with target parameter
    new_nodes = Skills.objects.build_tree_nodes(
        ml_expansion_data,
        target=machine_learning,
        position='last-child'
    )
    
    print(f"Built {len(new_nodes)} new nodes")
    Skills.objects.bulk_create(new_nodes)

print(f"Queries for adding subtree: {len(connection.queries)}")

print("\nUpdated Machine Learning branch:")

    indent = "  " * skill.level
