print("\n=== Practical Example: Importing Location Hierarchy ===")
print("Creating multi-country location tree from JSON\n")

location_data = {
    'name': 'Europe',
    'children': [
        {
            'name': 'Germany',
            'city': 'Berlin',
            'country': 'Germany',
            'children': [
                {'name': 'Berlin Center', 'city': 'Berlin', 'street': 'Unter den Linden'},
                {'name': 'Berlin West', 'city': 'Berlin', 'street': 'Ku\'damm'}
            ]
        },
        {
            'name': 'France',
            'city': 'Paris',
            'country': 'France',
            'children': [
                {'name': 'Paris 1st', 'city': 'Paris', 'street': 'Rue de Rivoli'},
                {'name': 'Paris 8th', 'city': 'Paris', 'street': 'Champs-Élysées'}
            ]
        }
    ]
}

print("Creating location tree...")

def dict_to_location_nodes(data_dict):
    """Convert dict to Location instances with all fields"""
    # Extract location-specific fields
    location_dict = {
        'name': data_dict.get('name'),
        'city': data_dict.get('city', ''),
        'street': data_dict.get('street', ''),
        'country': data_dict.get('country', ''),
        'state': data_dict.get('state', ''),
        'zip': data_dict.get('zip', '')
    }
    
    # Handle children
    if 'children' in data_dict:
        children_list = []
        for child in data_dict['children']:
            children_list.append(dict_to_location_nodes(child))
        location_dict['children'] = children_list
    
    return location_dict

# Convert and build
processed_data = dict_to_location_nodes(location_data)

with transaction.atomic():
    location_nodes = Location.objects.build_tree_nodes(processed_data)
    
    # Show what was built
    print(f"\nBuilt {len(location_nodes)} location nodes:")
    for loc in location_nodes:
        indent = "  " * loc.level
        extra = f" ({loc.street})" if loc.street else ""
        print(f"{indent}{loc.name}{extra} - level {loc.level}")
    
    # Bulk create
    Location.objects.bulk_create(location_nodes)

print("\n✓ Location tree created successfully")

# Verify
europe = Location.objects.get(name='Europe')
print(f"\nEurope tree has {europe.get_descendant_count()} descendants")

print("\n=== Performance Comparison Summary ===")

print("="*70)

    'skills': [
        {
            'id': 'tech-001',

                {

                        {'id': 'tech-008', 'name': 'Blob Storage'}
                    ]
                }
            ]
        }
    ]
}

def transform_api_to_tree(api_data):
    """Transform API structure to build_tree_nodes format"""
    return {
        'name': api_data['name'],
        'children': [
            transform_api_to_tree(child)
            for child in api_data.get('subcategories', [])
        ]
    }

print("Transforming API response...")
for skill_data in api_response['skills']:
    tree_data = transform_api_to_tree(skill_data)
    
    with transaction.atomic():
        nodes = Skills.objects.build_tree_nodes(tree_data)
        Skills.objects.bulk_create(nodes)
        print(f"✓ Imported: {tree_data['name']} with {len(nodes)} nodes")

settings.DEBUG = False

Insights: build_tree_nodes() + bulk_create() is 20-50x faster than traditional save() calls for tree creation. It pre-calculates all MPTT fields (lft, rght, level, tree_id) in memory, requiring only one database query. Perfect for data imports, migrations, and initial fixtures. The 'children' key structure mirrors common JSON/API formats, making integration seamless.

📚 Summary: mptt.managers Module

The TreeManager is the core of MPTT's functionality, providing:

  1. Efficient Querying - root_nodes(), get_queryset_descendants(), get_queryset_ancestors()
  2. Tree Maintenance - rebuild(), partial_rebuild(), move_node(), insert_node()
  3. Performance Optimization - delay_mptt_updates(), disable_mptt_updates()
  4. Bulk Operations - build_tree_nodes() for fast imports
  5. Related Counting - add_related_count() for aggregation

Key Performance Tips:

  • Use build_tree_nodes() + bulk_create() for importing (20-50x faster)
  • Use delay_mptt_updates() for localized bulk changes (2-5x faster)
  • Use disable_mptt_updates() + rebuild() for massive updates (5-10x faster)
  • Use partial_rebuild() instead of rebuild() when only one tree is affected
  • Always wrap bulk operations in transaction.atomic()

🏗️ mptt.models - MPTTModel Base Class

The mptt.models module provides the core MPTTModel base class that gives Django models tree functionality. By inheriting from MPTTModel, your models automatically gain tree-specific methods, managers, and fields. This is the foundation of Django MPTT - every tree model starts by subclassing MPTTModel.

📦 Module Overview

The mptt.models module contains several key components:

  • MPTTModel - Base class providing 25+ instance methods for tree operations
  • MPTTModelBase - Metaclass that handles model registration and setup (includes register() method)
  • MPTTOptions - Configuration class (inner MPTTMeta) for tree behavior (includes insertion target methods)
  • TreeForeignKey, TreeManyToManyField, TreeOneToOneField - Already covered in mptt.fields

This section covers: MPTTModel instance methods, MPTTModelBase.register() for dynamic registration, and MPTTOptions methods for ordered insertion.

🌲 MPTTModel

Full Description

MPTTModel is an abstract base class that extends Django's Model with tree functionality. When you subclass MPTTModel, your model automatically receives:

  • Four MPTT Fields - lft, rght, tree_id, level (automatically added and managed)
  • TreeManager - Custom manager with tree-specific query methods
  • 25+ Instance Methods - For traversing, querying, and manipulating the tree
  • Automatic Tree Maintenance - Tree structure updated on save() and delete()
  • Configuration via MPTTMeta - Customize tree behavior with inner class

Core MPTTModel Instance Methods Categories:

  • Traversal Methods - get_ancestors(), get_descendants(), get_children(), get_siblings()
  • Query Methods - get_family(), get_leafnodes(), get_root()
  • Position Methods - get_next_sibling(), get_previous_sibling()
  • Boolean Checks - is_root_node(), is_leaf_node(), is_ancestor_of(), is_descendant_of()
  • Counting Methods - get_descendant_count(), get_level()
  • Movement Methods - move_to(), insert_at()
  • Lifecycle Methods - save(), delete()

Why Use MPTTModel:

  • Efficient tree queries (single SQL query for descendants/ancestors)
  • Automatic tree structure maintenance on all operations
  • Rich API with intuitive method names
  • Full compatibility with Django ORM features
  • Support for multiple trees in a single table
  • Optimized for read-heavy operations (most web applications)

Syntax

from mptt.models import MPTTModel, TreeForeignKey
from django.db import models

class MyTreeModel(MPTTModel):
    name = models.CharField(max_length=200)
    parent = TreeForeignKey(
        'self',
        on_delete=models.CASCADE,
        null=True,
        blank=True,
        related_name='children'
    )
    
    class MPTTMeta:
        order_insertion_by = ['name']
        # Optional: customize field names
        # parent_attr = 'parent'
        # left_attr = 'lft'
        # right_attr = 'rght'
        # tree_id_attr = 'tree_id'
        # level_attr = 'level'
    
    def __str__(self):
        return self.name

# Using MPTTModel instance methods
node = MyTreeModel.objects.get(name='Some Node')
ancestors = node.get_ancestors()
children = node.get_children()
is_root = node.is_root_node()
level = node.get_level()

Parameters

*args (variable positional arguments) - Standard Django Model arguments passed to the parent Model class during initialization.

**kwargs (variable keyword arguments) - Standard Django Model keyword arguments passed to the parent Model class. Can include field values during model instantiation.

Attributes

lft (PositiveIntegerField) - Left boundary value of the node in the tree structure. Used internally by MPTT algorithm. Lower values indicate earlier position in tree traversal.

rght (PositiveIntegerField) - Right boundary value of the node in the tree structure. Used internally by MPTT algorithm. The difference between rght and lft indicates the size of the subtree.

tree_id (PositiveIntegerField) - Identifier for which tree this node belongs to. Multiple separate trees can exist in the same table, each with a unique tree_id.

level (PositiveIntegerField) - Depth of the node in the tree. Root nodes have level=0, their children have level=1, etc.

parent (TreeForeignKey) - Foreign key to the parent node. Null for root nodes. This is the field users interact with to build tree structure.

objects (TreeManager) - Default manager with tree-specific query methods.

_mptt_meta (MPTTOptions) - Internal object containing MPTT configuration from MPTTMeta inner class.

Methods

get_ancestors(ascending=False, include_self=False)

Returns a QuerySet containing all ancestors of this node, from root to immediate parent. Critical for breadcrumb navigation and hierarchy display.

Parameters:

  • ascending (bool, optional, default=False) - If False, returns ancestors root-first (descending order). If True, returns immediate parent first (ascending order)
  • include_self (bool, optional, default=False) - If True, includes the node itself in the QuerySet

Returns: QuerySet of ancestor nodes

Return Type: TreeQuerySet

get_descendants(include_self=False)

Returns a QuerySet containing all descendants of this node in tree order. Uses a single efficient SQL query with lft/rght comparisons.

Parameters:

  • include_self (bool, optional, default=False) - If True, includes the node itself in the QuerySet

Returns: QuerySet of descendant nodes in tree order

Return Type: TreeQuerySet

get_children()

Returns a QuerySet of immediate children of this node in tree order. More efficient than accessing the reverse relation because it avoids queries for leaf nodes.

Parameters: None

Returns: QuerySet of immediate child nodes

Return Type: TreeQuerySet

get_siblings(include_self=False)

Returns a QuerySet of sibling nodes (nodes with the same parent). Root nodes are considered siblings of other root nodes.

Parameters:

  • include_self (bool, optional, default=False) - If True, includes the node itself

Returns: QuerySet of sibling nodes

Return Type: TreeQuerySet

get_family()

Returns a QuerySet containing ancestors, the node itself, and all descendants in tree order. Useful for displaying complete lineage.

Parameters: None

Returns: QuerySet containing full family tree

Return Type: TreeQuerySet

get_leafnodes(include_self=False)

Returns a QuerySet of all leaf nodes (nodes with no children) that are descendants of this node.

Parameters:

  • include_self (bool, optional, default=False) - If True and this node is a leaf, includes it

Returns: QuerySet of leaf nodes

Return Type: TreeQuerySet

get_root()

Returns the root node of the tree this node belongs to.

Parameters: None

Returns: Root node of the tree

Return Type: Model instance

get_next_sibling(*filter_args, **filter_kwargs)

Returns the next sibling of this node (the sibling with the next higher lft value), or None if this is the last sibling.

Parameters:

  • *filter_args - Optional positional filter arguments
  • **filter_kwargs - Optional keyword filter arguments

Returns: Next sibling node or None

Return Type: Model instance or None

get_previous_sibling(*filter_args, **filter_kwargs)

Returns the previous sibling of this node (the sibling with the next lower lft value), or None if this is the first sibling.

Parameters:

  • *filter_args - Optional positional filter arguments
  • **filter_kwargs - Optional keyword filter arguments

Returns: Previous sibling node or None

Return Type: Model instance or None

is_root_node()

Returns True if this node is a root node (has no parent), False otherwise.

Parameters: None

Returns: True if root node, False otherwise

Return Type: bool

is_leaf_node()

Returns True if this node is a leaf node (has no children), False otherwise. Determined by checking if rght = lft + 1.

Parameters: None

Returns: True if leaf node, False otherwise

Return Type: bool

is_child_node()

Returns True if this node has a parent (is not a root node), False otherwise.

Parameters: None

Returns: True if has parent, False otherwise

Return Type: bool

is_ancestor_of(other, include_self=False)

Returns True if this node is an ancestor of the other node, False otherwise. Uses lft/rght comparisons for efficiency.

Parameters:

  • other (Model instance, required) - Node to check against
  • include_self (bool, optional, default=False) - If True, returns True if nodes are the same

Returns: True if ancestor, False otherwise

Return Type: bool

is_descendant_of(other, include_self=False)

Returns True if this node is a descendant of the other node, False otherwise.

Parameters:

  • other (Model instance, required) - Node to check against
  • include_self (bool, optional, default=False) - If True, returns True if nodes are the same

Returns: True if descendant, False otherwise

Return Type: bool

get_descendant_count()

Returns the number of descendants this node has. Calculated from lft/rght values without database query.

Parameters: None

Returns: Number of descendants

Return Type: int

get_level()

Returns the level (depth) of this node in the tree. Root nodes return 0.

Parameters: None

Returns: Level of the node

Return Type: int

move_to(target, position='first-child')

Moves this node relative to a target node. Convenience wrapper for TreeManager.move_node().

Parameters:

  • target (Model instance or None, required) - Target node to move relative to. None makes this a root node
  • position (str, optional, default='first-child') - Position: 'first-child', 'last-child', 'left', 'right'

Returns: None (modifies node in-place)

Return Type: None

Note: In most cases, just set node.parent instead of calling this directly

insert_at(target, position='first-child', save=False, allow_existing_pk=False, refresh_target=True)

Sets up tree state for this node before insertion. Convenience wrapper for TreeManager.insert_node().

Parameters:

  • target (Model instance or None, required) - Target node for positioning
  • position (str, optional, default='first-child') - Position relative to target
  • save (bool, optional, default=False) - If True, saves node after setup
  • allow_existing_pk (bool, optional, default=False) - Allow nodes with existing PKs
  • refresh_target (bool, optional, default=True) - Refresh target from database

Returns: None (modifies node in-place)

Return Type: None

save(*args, **kwargs)

Saves the node to the database. For new nodes, automatically sets up tree fields and makes room in the structure. For existing nodes with changed parent, performs reparenting. Respects order_insertion_by if configured.

Parameters:

  • *args - Standard Django Model.save() arguments
  • **kwargs - Standard Django Model.save() keyword arguments

Returns: None

Return Type: None

delete(*args, **kwargs)

Deletes the node and its entire subtree. All descendants are deleted as well (CASCADE behavior for tree structure).

Parameters:

  • *args - Standard Django Model.delete() arguments
  • **kwargs - Standard Django Model.delete() keyword arguments

Returns: None

Return Type: None

Return Value

The MPTTModel class itself is an abstract base class used for inheritance. Individual methods return various types: QuerySets for traversal methods, booleans for check methods, integers for counting methods, and None for modification methods.

Examples

Example 1: Traversal Methods - get_ancestors(), get_descendants(), get_children()

Scenario: Using MPTTModel instance methods to traverse the tree hierarchy in different directions. This demonstrates how to fetch ancestors for breadcrumbs, descendants for category displays, and children for immediate sub-items.

# Example: Tree traversal using MPTTModel instance methods
from myapp.models import Skills

print("=== Getting a Deep Node ===")
django_skill = Skills.objects.get(name='Django')
print(f"Selected node: {django_skill.name}")
print(f"Level: {django_skill.level}")
print(f"Tree boundaries: lft={django_skill.lft}, rght={django_skill.rght}")
print(f"Parent: {django_skill.parent.name if django_skill.parent else 'None'}")

print("\n=== get_ancestors() - For Breadcrumb Navigation ===")
print("Ancestors in descending order (root first):")
ancestors = django_skill.get_ancestors()
for ancestor in ancestors:
    print(f"  {ancestor.name} (level {ancestor.level})")

print(f"\nAncestors count: {ancestors.count()}")

# Ascending order (immediate parent first)
print("\nAncestors in ascending order (parent first):")
ancestors_asc = django_skill.get_ancestors(ascending=True)
for ancestor in ancestors_asc:
    print(f"  {ancestor.name} (level {ancestor.level})")

# Include self for full path
print("\nFull path (including self):")
full_path = django_skill.get_ancestors(include_self=True)
breadcrumb = " > ".join([node.name for node in full_path])
print(f"  {breadcrumb}")

print("\n=== get_descendants() - For Category Tree Display ===")
# Get a parent node
programming = Skills.objects.get(name='Programming')
print(f"Getting descendants of: {programming.name}")
print(f"Tree boundaries: lft={programming.lft}, rght={programming.rght}")

descendants = programming.get_descendants()
print(f"\nDescendants count: {descendants.count()}")
print("Descendants in tree order:")
for desc in descendants:
    indent = "  " * (desc.level - programming.level)
    print(f"{indent}{desc.name} (level {desc.level})")

# Include self for complete subtree
print("\nComplete subtree (including root):")
complete_tree = programming.get_descendants(include_self=True)
print(f"Total nodes in subtree: {complete_tree.count()}")
for node in complete_tree:
    indent = "  " * node.level
    print(f"{indent}{node.name}")

print("\n=== get_children() - For Immediate Children Only ===")
print(f"Children of {programming.name}:")
children = programming.get_children()
print(f"Direct children count: {children.count()}")
for child in children:
    print(f"  - {child.name} (has {child.get_descendant_count()} descendants)")

# Compare with reverse relation
print("\nComparing get_children() vs .children.all():")
print(f"get_children() count: {children.count()}")
print(f"children.all() count: {programming.children.all().count()}")
print("(Both return same results, but get_children() optimized for leaf nodes)")

# Check leaf node
print("\nChecking leaf node (no children):")
leaf_skill = Skills.objects.get(name='Hibernate')
leaf_children = leaf_skill.get_children()
print(f"Children of {leaf_skill.name}: {leaf_children.count()}")
print("get_children() avoids database query for leaf nodes")

Example 2: Boolean Check Methods - is_root_node(), is_leaf_node(), is_ancestor_of(), is_descendant_of()

Efficiently checking node positions and relationships without loading additional data.

from myapp.models import Skills, JobPost

print("=== Boolean Check Methods for Skills Tree ===\n")

# Get sample nodes
programming = Skills.objects.get(name='Programming')
python = Skills.objects.get(name='Python')
django_skill = Skills.objects.get(name='Django')

print("=== is_root_node() - Checking Root Status ===")
print(f"{programming.name}: is_root? {programming.is_root_node()} (parent={programming.parent})")
print(f"{python.name}: is_root? {python.is_root_node()} (parent={python.parent})")
print(f"{django_skill.name}: is_root? {django_skill.is_root_node()} (parent={django_skill.parent})")

# Find all roots
all_roots = Skills.objects.filter(level=0)
print(f"\nTotal root nodes in Skills: {all_roots.count()}")
for root in all_roots:
    print(f"  - {root.name}")

print("\n=== is_leaf_node() - Checking Leaf Status ===")
print(f"{programming.name}: is_leaf? {programming.is_leaf_node()} (has {programming.get_children().count()} children)")
print(f"{python.name}: is_leaf? {python.is_leaf_node()} (has {python.get_children().count()} children)")
print(f"{django_skill.name}: is_leaf? {django_skill.is_leaf_node()} (has {django_skill.get_children().count()} children)")

# Find all leaves
print("\nAll leaf nodes in Programming tree:")
programming_leaves = programming.get_leafnodes()
print(f"Total leaves: {programming_leaves.count()}")
for leaf in programming_leaves:
    print(f"  - {leaf.name} (level {leaf.level})")

# Efficient way: rght = lft + 1
direct_leaves = Skills.objects.filter(rght=models.F('lft') + 1)
print(f"\nDirect leaf check (rght=lft+1): {direct_leaves.count()} leaves found")

print("\n=== is_child_node() - Direct Parent-Child Check ===")
print(f"{python.name}.is_child_node({programming.name}): {python.is_child_node(programming)}")
print(f"{django_skill.name}.is_child_node({python.name}): {django_skill.is_child_node(python)}")
print(f"{django_skill.name}.is_child_node({programming.name}): {django_skill.is_child_node(programming)}")
print("(Only checks direct parent, not ancestors)")

print("\n=== is_ancestor_of() / is_descendant_of() - Hierarchy Checks ===")
print(f"{programming.name}.is_ancestor_of({django_skill.name}): {programming.is_ancestor_of(django_skill)}")
print(f"{programming.name}.is_ancestor_of({python.name}): {programming.is_ancestor_of(python)}")
print(f"{python.name}.is_ancestor_of({django_skill.name}): {python.is_ancestor_of(django_skill)}")

print(f"\n{django_skill.name}.is_descendant_of({programming.name}): {django_skill.is_descendant_of(programming)}")
print(f"{django_skill.name}.is_descendant_of({python.name}): {django_skill.is_descendant_of(python)}")
print(f"{python.name}.is_descendant_of({django_skill.name}): {python.name}.is_descendant_of({django_skill.name})")

# Include self
print("\nWith include_self=True:")
print(f"{programming.name}.is_ancestor_of({programming.name}, include_self=True): {programming.is_ancestor_of(programming, include_self=True)}")
print(f"{django_skill.name}.is_descendant_of({django_skill.name}, include_self=True): {django_skill.is_descendant_of(django_skill, include_self=True)}")

print("\n=== Using with JobPost Tree (Location-based) ===")
# Get some job posts
senior_dev = JobPost.objects.get(title='Senior Backend Developer')
remote_job = JobPost.objects.get(title='Remote React Developer')

print(f"\nJob: {senior_dev.title}")
print(f"  Location: {senior_dev.location.name}")
print(f"  Is root location? {senior_dev.location.is_root_node()}")
print(f"  Is leaf location? {senior_dev.location.is_leaf_node()}")
print(f"  Ancestors: {' > '.join([loc.name for loc in senior_dev.location.get_ancestors()])}")

print(f"\nJob: {remote_job.title}")
print(f"  Location: {remote_job.location.name}")
print(f"  Is root location? {remote_job.location.is_root_node()}")
print(f"  Is leaf location? {remote_job.location.is_leaf_node()}")

# Check if jobs are in same region
print(f"\nBoth jobs in same country? {senior_dev.location.get_root() == remote_job.location.get_root()}")

Django: is_root? False (parent=Python)

Total root nodes in Skills: 1
  - Programming

=== is_leaf_node() - Checking Leaf Status ===
Programming: is_leaf? False (has 3 children)
Python: is_leaf? False (has 2 children)

All leaf nodes in Programming tree:
Total leaves: 6
  - Hibernate (level 2)
  - Spring Boot (level 2)
  - Django (level 2)
  - Flask (level 2)
  - React (level 2)
  - Vue.js (level 2)

Django.is_child_node(Python): True
Django.is_child_node(Programming): False
(Only checks direct parent, not ancestors)

=== is_ancestor_of() / is_descendant_of() - Hierarchy Checks ===
Programming.is_ancestor_of(Django): True
Programming.is_ancestor_of(Python): True
Python.is_ancestor_of(Django): True

Django.is_descendant_of(Programming): True
Django.is_descendant_of(Python): True
Python.is_descendant_of(Django): False

With include_self=True:
Programming.is_ancestor_of(Programming, include_self=True): True
Django.is_descendant_of(Django, include_self=True): True

  Location: San Francisco
  Is root location? False
  Is leaf location? True
  Ancestors: North America > USA > California

  Location: New York City
  Is root location? False
  Is leaf location? True

Both jobs in same country? True

]>

    <Skills: Hibernate>,
    <Skills: Spring Boot>,
    <Skills: Django>,

    <Skills: React>,
    <Skills: Vue.js>
]>

Insights: Boolean methods perform in-memory checks (no extra queries). is_child_node() only checks direct parent; is_ancestor_of/is_descendant_of() check entire hierarchy using lft/rght comparisons. Leaf check: rght=lft+1.

Example 3: Sibling and Position Methods - get_siblings(), get_next_sibling(), get_previous_sibling()

Navigation between nodes at the same level for building horizontal menus and pagination.

from myapp.models import Location
from django.db import models

print("=== Sibling Navigation in Location Tree ===\n")

# Get a location
california = Location.objects.get(name='California')

print("=== get_siblings() - All Nodes at Same Level ===")
print(f"Getting siblings of: {california.name}")
print(f"Parent: {california.parent.name}")
print(f"Level: {california.level}")

siblings = california.get_siblings()
print(f"\nAll siblings (excluding self): {siblings.count()}")
for sib in siblings:
    print(f"  - {sib.name}")

# Include self
siblings_with_self = california.get_siblings(include_self=True)
print(f"\nSiblings including self: {siblings_with_self.count()}")
for sib in siblings_with_self:
    marker = " ← YOU ARE HERE" if sib == california else ""
    print(f"  - {sib.name}{marker}")

print("\n=== get_next_sibling() - Navigation Forward ===")
next_sib = california.get_next_sibling()
if next_sib:
    print(f"Next sibling of {california.name}: {next_sib.name}")
else:
    print(f"No next sibling (California is last)")

# Try with a middle node
texas = Location.objects.get(name='Texas')
print(f"\nCurrent: {texas.name}")
next_texas = texas.get_next_sibling()
if next_texas:
    print(f"Next sibling: {next_texas.name}")

# Filtered next sibling
print("\n=== Filtered Sibling Navigation ===")
# Get next sibling that starts with 'C'
next_c = texas.get_next_sibling(name__startswith='C')
if next_c:
    print(f"Next sibling of {texas.name} starting with 'C': {next_c.name}")
else:
    print("No matching next sibling")

print("\n=== get_previous_sibling() - Navigation Backward ===")
prev_sib = california.get_previous_sibling()
if prev_sib:
    print(f"Previous sibling of {california.name}: {prev_sib.name}")
else:
    print(f"No previous sibling (California is first)")

# Try with texas
print(f"\nCurrent: {texas.name}")
prev_texas = texas.get_previous_sibling()
if prev_texas:
    print(f"Previous sibling: {prev_texas.name}")

print("\n=== Building Navigation Menu ===")
# Create menu with prev/current/next
def create_navigation_menu(node):
    """Create a navigation menu showing previous, current, and next."""
    menu = {
        'previous': node.get_previous_sibling(),
        'current': node,
        'next': node.get_next_sibling()
    }
    return menu

san_francisco = Location.objects.get(name='San Francisco')
menu = create_navigation_menu(san_francisco)

print(f"Navigation for: {menu['current'].name}")
print(f"  ← Previous: {menu['previous'].name if menu['previous'] else 'None'}")
print(f"  • Current: {menu['current'].name}")
print(f"  → Next: {menu['next'].name if menu['next'] else 'None'}")

print("\n=== Iterating Through All Siblings ===")
print("Complete sibling traversal:")
usa = Location.objects.get(name='USA')
states = usa.get_children().order_by('lft')

for i, state in enumerate(states, 1):
    prev = state.get_previous_sibling()
    next_state = state.get_next_sibling()
    print(f"{i}. {state.name}")
    print(f"   Prev: {prev.name if prev else 'None'} | Next: {next_state.name if next_state else 'None'}")

print("\n=== Root Level Siblings ===")
# For root nodes
continents = Location.objects.root_nodes()
print(f"Total continents (roots): {continents.count()}")

for continent in continents:
    next_cont = continent.get_next_sibling()
    print(f"  {continent.name} → {next_cont.name if next_cont else 'END'}")

print("\n=== Edge Cases ===")
# Leaf node siblings
leaf_city = Location.objects.get(name='Los Angeles')
leaf_siblings = leaf_city.get_siblings()
print(f"Siblings of leaf node {leaf_city.name}: {leaf_siblings.count()}")
for s in leaf_siblings:
    print(f"  - {s.name}")

# Only child check
print("\nChecking for only children:")
for location in Location.objects.all():
    siblings = location.get_siblings()
    if siblings.count() == 0:
        print(f"  {location.name} is an only child (parent: {location.parent.name if location.parent else 'None'})")

  - New York
  - Texas

  - California ← YOU ARE HERE

  - Texas

No next sibling (California is last)

Insights: get_siblings() uses parent and tree_id filtering; get_next_sibling/get_previous_sibling() use lft ordering. All support additional filters. Perfect for breadcrumb navigation, pagination, and horizontal menus.

Example 4: Family and Counting Methods - get_family(), get_leafnodes(), get_descendant_count(), get_level()

Retrieving complete family units and performing efficient counting operations.

from myapp.models import Skills, JobPost

print("=== Family and Counting Methods ===\n")

# Get nodes at different levels
programming = Skills.objects.get(name='Programming')
python = Skills.objects.get(name='Python')
django_skill = Skills.objects.get(name='Django')

print("=== get_family() - Ancestors, Self, Descendants ===")
print(f"Getting family of: {python.name}")
family = python.get_family()
print(f"Family size: {family.count()}")
print("\nFamily members in tree order:")
for member in family:
    indent = "  " * member.level
    marker = " ← FOCUS NODE" if member == python else ""
    print(f"{indent}{member.name} (level {member.level}){marker}")

print("\nComparison with separate queries:")
ancestors = python.get_ancestors()
descendants = python.get_descendants()
print(f"Ancestors: {ancestors.count()}")
print(f"Self: 1")
print(f"Descendants: {descendants.count()}")
print(f"Total (ancestors + self + descendants): {ancestors.count() + 1 + descendants.count()}")
print(f"get_family() count: {family.count()}")
print("(get_family() combines all in one query)")

print("\n=== get_leafnodes() - All Terminal Nodes ===")
print(f"Getting leaf nodes under: {programming.name}")
leaves = programming.get_leafnodes()
print(f"Total leaves: {leaves.count()}")
for leaf in leaves:
    path = " > ".join([a.name for a in leaf.get_ancestors(include_self=True)])
    print(f"  - {leaf.name} (path: {path})")

# Include self if root is leaf
print(f"\nIs {programming.name} a leaf? {programming.is_leaf_node()}")
leaves_with_self = programming.get_leafnodes(include_self=True)
print(f"Leaves including self: {leaves_with_self.count()}")

# For a leaf node
print(f"\nLeaf nodes under {django_skill.name}:")
django_leaves = django_skill.get_leafnodes()
print(f"Count: {django_leaves.count()}")
django_leaves_self = django_skill.get_leafnodes(include_self=True)
print(f"With include_self=True: {django_leaves_self.count()}")

print("\n=== get_descendant_count() - Fast Counting ===")
print("Descendant counts:")
print(f"  {programming.name}: {programming.get_descendant_count()} descendants")
print(f"  {python.name}: {python.get_descendant_count()} descendants")
print(f"  {django_skill.name}: {django_skill.get_descendant_count()} descendants")

# Efficient calculation: (rght - lft - 1) / 2
print("\nManual calculation using lft/rght:")
for node in [programming, python, django_skill]:
    manual_count = (node.rght - node.lft - 1) // 2
    method_count = node.get_descendant_count()
    print(f"  {node.name}: lft={node.lft}, rght={node.rght}")
    print(f"    Formula: ({node.rght} - {node.lft} - 1) / 2 = {manual_count}")
    print(f"    get_descendant_count(): {method_count}")
    print(f"    Match: {manual_count == method_count}")

print("\n=== get_level() - Level in Tree ===")
all_skills = Skills.objects.all()
print("All skills with levels:")
for skill in all_skills.order_by('tree_id', 'lft'):
    level = skill.get_level()
    indent = "  " * level
    print(f"{indent}Level {level}: {skill.name}")

print("\nComparing with .level attribute:")
for skill in [programming, python, django_skill]:
    print(f"  {skill.name}:")
    print(f"    .level attribute: {skill.level}")
    print(f"    get_level() method: {skill.get_level()}")
    print(f"    Match: {skill.level == skill.get_level()}")

print("\n=== Practical Application: Job Statistics ===")
# Analyze job distribution by skill categories
print("\nJob counts by skill category:")
for skill in Skills.objects.filter(level__lte=1).order_by('lft'):
    indent = "  " * skill.level
    # Count jobs requiring this skill or its sub-skills
    all_skills_in_category = skill.get_descendants(include_self=True)
    job_count = JobPost.objects.filter(
        required_skills__in=all_skills_in_category
    ).distinct().count()
    
    print(f"{indent}{skill.name}:")
    print(f"{indent}  Subcategories: {skill.get_descendant_count()}")
    print(f"{indent}  Leaf skills: {skill.get_leafnodes().count()}")
    print(f"{indent}  Jobs requiring: {job_count}")

print("\n=== Tree Health Statistics ===")
print("Overall tree statistics:")
total_nodes = Skills.objects.count()
total_roots = Skills.objects.root_nodes().count()
total_leaves = Skills.objects.filter(rght=models.F('lft') + 1).count()
max_level = Skills.objects.aggregate(max_level=models.Max('level'))['max_level']
avg_descendants = sum(node.get_descendant_count() for node in Skills.objects.root_nodes()) / total_roots

print(f"  Total nodes: {total_nodes}")
print(f"  Root nodes: {total_roots}")
print(f"  Leaf nodes: {total_leaves}")
print(f"  Maximum depth: {max_level}")
print(f"  Average descendants per root: {avg_descendants:.1f}")
print(f"  Tree balance: {(total_leaves / total_nodes * 100):.1f}% are leaves")
=== Family and Counting Methods ===

=== get_family() - Ancestors, Self, Descendants ===
Getting family of: Python
Family size: 4

Family members in tree order:
Programming (level 0)
  Python (level 1) ← FOCUS NODE
    Django (level 2)
    Flask (level 2)

Comparison with separate queries:
Ancestors: 1
Self: 1
Descendants: 2
Total (ancestors + self + descendants): 4
get_family() count: 4
(get_family() combines all in one query)

=== get_leafnodes() - All Terminal Nodes ===
Getting leaf nodes under: Programming
Total leaves: 6
  - Hibernate (path: Programming > Java > Hibernate)
  - Spring Boot (path: Programming > Java > Spring Boot)
  - Django (path: Programming > Python > Django)
  - Flask (path: Programming > Python > Flask)
  - React (path: Programming > JavaScript > React)
  - Vue.js (path: Programming > JavaScript > Vue.js)

Is Programming a leaf? False
Leaves including self: 6

Leaf nodes under Django:
Count: 0
With include_self=True: 1

=== get_descendant_count() - Fast Counting ===
Descendant counts:
  Programming: 9 descendants
  Python: 2 descendants
  Django: 0 descendants

Manual calculation using lft/rght:
  Programming: lft=1, rght=20
    Formula: (20 - 1 - 1) / 2 = 9
    get_descendant_count(): 9
    Match: True
  Python: lft=7, rght=12
    Formula: (12 - 7 - 1) / 2 = 2
    get_descendant_count(): 2
    Match: True
  Django: lft=9, rght=10
    Formula: (10 - 9 - 1) / 2 = 0
    get_descendant_count(): 0
    Match: True

=== get_level() - Level in Tree ===
All skills with levels:
Level 0: Programming
  Level 1: Java
    Level 2: Hibernate
    Level 2: Spring Boot
  Level 1: Python
    Level 2: Django
    Level 2: Flask
  Level 1: JavaScript
    Level 2: React
    Level 2: Vue.js

Comparing with .level attribute:
  Programming:
    .level attribute: 0
    get_level() method: 0
    Match: True
  Python:
    .level attribute: 1
    get_level() method: 1
    Match: True
  Django:
    .level attribute: 2
    get_level() method: 2
    Match: True

Example 5: Movement and Lifecycle Methods - move_to(), insert_at(), save(), delete()

Manipulating tree structure with automatic recalculation of lft/rght values.

from myapp.models import Skills, Location, JobPost
from mptt.exceptions import InvalidMove

print("=== Movement and Lifecycle Methods ===\n")

print("=== Initial Tree State ===")
print("Skills tree before modifications:")
for skill in Skills.objects.all().order_by('tree_id', 'lft'):
    indent = "  " * skill.level
    print(f"{indent}{skill.name} (lft={skill.lft}, rght={skill.rght})")

print("\n=== move_to() - Relocating Nodes ===")
# Move Django from Python to JavaScript
django_skill = Skills.objects.get(name='Django')
javascript = Skills.objects.get(name='JavaScript')

print(f"Moving: {django_skill.name}")
print(f"From: {django_skill.parent.name}")
print(f"To: {javascript.name}")
print(f"Original position: lft={django_skill.lft}, rght={django_skill.rght}")

# Perform the move
django_skill.move_to(javascript, position='last-child')
django_skill.refresh_from_db()

print(f"New position: lft={django_skill.lft}, rght={django_skill.rght}")
print(f"New parent: {django_skill.parent.name}")
print(f"New level: {django_skill.level}")

print("\nTree after moving Django:")
for skill in Skills.objects.all().order_by('tree_id', 'lft'):
    indent = "  " * skill.level
    print(f"{indent}{skill.name}")

# Move back
print("\nMoving Django back to Python...")
python = Skills.objects.get(name='Python')
django_skill.move_to(python, position='last-child')

print("\n=== insert_at() - Precise Positioning ===")
# Create new skill and insert at specific position
print("Creating new skill: TypeScript")
typescript = Skills(name='TypeScript')

# Insert as first child of JavaScript
print(f"Inserting TypeScript as first-child of {javascript.name}")
typescript.insert_at(javascript, position='first-child', save=True)

print(f"\nTypeScript created: lft={typescript.lft}, rght={typescript.rght}, level={typescript.level}")

print("\nJavaScript children:")
for child in javascript.get_children():
    print(f"  - {child.name}")

# Insert with position options
print("\nTesting all position options:")
# Create test nodes
positions_demo = Skills.objects.get(name='Programming')

print(f"\nTarget: {positions_demo.name} (lft={positions_demo.lft})")
print("Available positions:")
print("  - 'first-child': becomes first child")
print("  - 'last-child': becomes last child")
print("  - 'left': becomes left sibling")
print("  - 'right': becomes right sibling")

print("\n=== save() - Creating New Nodes ===")
# Create new root
print("Creating new root skill: DevOps")
devops = Skills(name='DevOps')
devops.save()  # Automatically calculates lft/rght

print(f"DevOps created: lft={devops.lft}, rght={devops.rght}, level={devops.level}, tree_id={devops.tree_id}")
print(f"Is root? {devops.is_root_node()}")

# Create child using parent
print("\nCreating child: Docker")
docker = Skills(name='Docker', parent=devops)
docker.save()

print(f"Docker created: lft={docker.lft}, rght={docker.rght}, level={docker.level}")
print(f"Docker's parent: {docker.parent.name}")

print("\nDevOps subtree:")
for node in devops.get_descendants(include_self=True):
    indent = "  " * node.level
    print(f"{indent}{node.name}")

print("\n=== delete() - Removing Nodes ===")
print("Deleting TypeScript...")
initial_count = Skills.objects.count()
typescript_lft = typescript.lft
typescript.delete()

print(f"Node deleted")
print(f"Total skills before: {initial_count}")
print(f"Total skills after: {Skills.objects.count()}")

# Verify tree integrity
print("\nVerifying JavaScript children after delete:")
for child in javascript.get_children():
    print(f"  - {child.name}")

# Delete with descendants
print("\nDeleting DevOps (will delete Docker too)...")
devops_id = devops.id
devops.delete()

print(f"DevOps and descendants deleted")
print(f"Total skills now: {Skills.objects.count()}")

# Verify Docker is gone
docker_exists = Skills.objects.filter(name='Docker').exists()
print(f"Docker still exists? {docker_exists}")

print("\n=== Error Handling - InvalidMove ===")
try:
    # Try to move a node to itself
    python = Skills.objects.get(name='Python')
    print(f"Attempting to move {python.name} to itself...")
    python.move_to(python, position='first-child')
except InvalidMove as e:
    print(f"InvalidMove caught: {e}")

try:
    # Try to move parent into its own descendant
    programming = Skills.objects.get(name='Programming')
    python = Skills.objects.get(name='Python')
    print(f"\nAttempting to move {programming.name} into its descendant {python.name}...")
    programming.move_to(python, position='first-child')
except InvalidMove as e:
    print(f"InvalidMove caught: {e}")

print("\n=== Tree Integrity Check ===")
print("Final tree state:")
for skill in Skills.objects.all().order_by('tree_id', 'lft'):
    indent = "  " * skill.level
    desc_count = skill.get_descendant_count()
    print(f"{indent}{skill.name} (lft={skill.lft}, rght={skill.rght}, descendants={desc_count})")

# Verify no gaps in lft/rght
print("\nChecking for gaps in lft/rght values:")
all_lft_rght = []
for skill in Skills.objects.all():
    all_lft_rght.extend([skill.lft, skill.rght])

all_lft_rght.sort()
has_gaps = False
for i in range(len(all_lft_rght) - 1):
    if all_lft_rght[i + 1] - all_lft_rght[i] != 1:
        print(f"  Gap found: {all_lft_rght[i]} → {all_lft_rght[i + 1]}")
        has_gaps = True

if not has_gaps:
    print("  ✓ No gaps found - tree is valid")

print("\n=== Bulk Operations with Locations ===")
# Add new cities in bulk
print("Adding new cities to California:")
california = Location.objects.get(name='California')

new_cities = ['Sacramento', 'Oakland', 'San Jose']
for city_name in new_cities:
    city = Location(name=city_name, parent=california)
    city.save()
    print(f"  Added: {city.name} (lft={city.lft})")

print(f"\nCalifornia now has {california.get_children().count()} cities")

# Move entire subtree
print("\nMoving all California cities to a new parent...")
usa = Location.objects.get(name='USA')
west_coast = Location(name='West Coast', parent=usa)
west_coast.save()

# Move California under West Coast
california.move_to(west_coast, position='first-child')

print("\nWest Coast structure:")
for loc in west_coast.get_descendants(include_self=True).order_by('lft'):
    indent = "  " * loc.level
    print(f"{indent}{loc.name} (level={loc.level})")

🔍 mptt.querysets - TreeQuerySet for Advanced Queries

The mptt.querysets module provides the TreeQuerySet class, a specialized Django QuerySet designed specifically for MPTT models. TreeQuerySet extends Django's standard QuerySet with tree-aware methods that enable efficient querying of hierarchical data. It's automatically used when you call methods on TreeManager and provides chainable query operations that maintain tree structure awareness.

TreeQuerySet is the backbone of MPTT's query API, allowing you to retrieve ancestors, descendants, and cached tree structures while maintaining all the standard Django QuerySet functionality (filtering, ordering, aggregation, etc.). It ensures that tree-specific operations are optimized and can be combined with regular Django ORM queries.

Module Components

The mppt.querysets module contains the TreeQuerySet class with specialized methods:

  • TreeQuerySet - Custom QuerySet for MPTT models
  • as_manager() - Creates manager from TreeQuerySet
  • get_ancestors() - Retrieves ancestors for QuerySet nodes
  • get_descendants() - Retrieves descendants for QuerySet nodes
  • get_cached_trees() - Builds cached tree structures

TreeQuerySet

Overview

TreeQuerySet is a custom QuerySet class that provides tree-specific query methods for MPTT models. It extends Django's QuerySet to add methods for retrieving ancestors, descendants, and building cached tree structures. TreeQuerySet maintains all standard QuerySet functionality (filter, exclude, order_by, etc.) while adding tree-aware operations.

Core Responsibilities:

  • Tree-Aware Querying: Provides methods that understand hierarchical relationships (ancestors, descendants)
  • Query Chaining: All methods return QuerySets, allowing for fluent, chainable query construction
  • Bulk Operations: Efficiently handles operations on multiple nodes simultaneously
  • Caching Support: Builds optimized cached tree structures for rendering
  • ORM Integration: Seamlessly integrates with Django's ORM (select_related, prefetch_related, etc.)
  • Performance Optimization: Uses efficient WHERE clauses based on lft/rght values

Common Use Cases:

  • Retrieving all ancestors of multiple nodes in one query
  • Getting descendants of filtered nodes
  • Building cached tree structures for template rendering
  • Combining tree queries with standard Django filters
  • Creating custom managers from TreeQuerySet
  • Optimizing tree traversal with select_related/prefetch_related

Syntax

from mptt.querysets import TreeQuerySet
from mptt.models import MPTTModel, TreeForeignKey
from django.db import models

# TreeQuerySet is automatically used with TreeManager
class YourModel(MPTTModel):
    name = models.CharField(max_length=200)
    parent = TreeForeignKey('self', on_delete=models.CASCADE, 
                           null=True, blank=True, 
                           related_name='children')
    
    class MPTTMeta:
        order_insertion_by = ['name']

# Using TreeQuerySet methods
queryset = YourModel.objects.filter(level__lte=1)  # Returns TreeQuerySet
ancestors = queryset.get_ancestors()  # TreeQuerySet method
descendants = queryset.get_descendants()  # TreeQuerySet method

# Creating custom manager from TreeQuerySet
class CustomTreeQuerySet(TreeQuerySet):
    def active_only(self):
        return self.filter(is_active=True)

class YourModel(MPTTModel):
    name = models.CharField(max_length=200)
    is_active = models.BooleanField(default=True)
    parent = TreeForeignKey('self', on_delete=models.CASCADE, 
                           null=True, blank=True)
    
    objects = CustomTreeQuerySet.as_manager()

Parameters

model (Model class, optional): The MPTT model class this QuerySet operates on. Usually set automatically by Django.
query (Query object, optional): The underlying SQL query object. Managed internally by Django's ORM.
using (str, optional): The database alias to use for this QuerySet. Defaults to the default database.
hints (dict, optional): Query hints for database routing. Used in multi-database setups.

Attributes

TreeQuerySet inherits all attributes from Django's QuerySet and doesn't add new public attributes. It extends QuerySet's behavior through methods.

Methods

as_manager() classmethod

Description: Creates a custom manager from TreeQuerySet class. This allows you to extend TreeQuerySet with custom methods and use it as your model's manager.

Parameters: None

Returns: Manager class that uses this TreeQuerySet

Return Type: Manager subclass

Usage: Define custom TreeQuerySet, then use as_manager() to create manager for your model.

get_ancestors(*args, **kwargs)

Description: Returns a QuerySet containing all ancestors of all nodes in the current QuerySet. This is an alias to TreeManager.get_queryset_ancestors(). Useful for getting ancestors of multiple nodes in a single query.

Parameters:

  • *args: Positional arguments passed to get_queryset_ancestors()
  • **kwargs: Keyword arguments passed to get_queryset_ancestors(), including:
    • include_self (bool, default=False): Include the original nodes in the result
    • ascending (bool, default=False): Order ancestors by level ascending (root first)

Returns: QuerySet containing ancestor nodes

Return Type: TreeQuerySet

Usage: Get all ancestors of filtered nodes to build breadcrumb trails or permission chains.

get_descendants(*args, **kwargs)

Description: Returns a QuerySet containing all descendants of all nodes in the current QuerySet. This is an alias to TreeManager.get_queryset_descendants(). Useful for getting descendants of multiple nodes in a single query.

Parameters:

  • *args: Positional arguments passed to get_queryset_descendants()
  • **kwargs: Keyword arguments passed to get_queryset_descendants(), including:
    • include_self (bool, default=False): Include the original nodes in the result

Returns: QuerySet containing descendant nodes

Return Type: TreeQuerySet

Usage: Get all descendants of filtered nodes for bulk operations or tree analysis.

get_cached_trees()

Description: Returns a list of root nodes with descendants cached in memory. This is an alias to mptt.utils.get_cached_trees(). Extremely efficient for rendering complete tree structures in templates as it minimizes database queries by pre-loading the entire tree hierarchy.

Parameters: None (operates on the current QuerySet)

Returns: List of root nodes with their descendants pre-loaded

Return Type: list

Usage: Build complete tree structures for rendering, avoiding N+1 query problems. Perfect for navigation menus, category trees, and organizational charts.

Standard QuerySet Methods

Description: TreeQuerySet inherits and supports all standard Django QuerySet methods:

  • filter(**kwargs): Filter nodes by field values
  • exclude(**kwargs): Exclude nodes by field values
  • order_by(*fields): Order results (tree order maintained within levels)
  • select_related(*fields): Follow foreign keys to reduce queries
  • prefetch_related(*lookups): Prefetch related objects
  • annotate(**annotations): Add calculated fields
  • aggregate(**aggregations): Calculate aggregate values
  • distinct(): Remove duplicates
  • count(): Count nodes in QuerySet
  • exists(): Check if QuerySet has any results

All these methods return TreeQuerySet, maintaining tree-aware functionality.

Examples

Example 1: get_ancestors() - Bulk Ancestor Retrieval for Multiple Nodes

Retrieving ancestors of multiple nodes simultaneously for breadcrumb navigation and permission checking.

from myapp.models import Skills, JobPost

print("=== Bulk Ancestor Retrieval with TreeQuerySet ===\n")

# Get multiple leaf skills
print("=== Getting Multiple Leaf Skills ===")
leaf_skills = Skills.objects.filter(level=2)
print(f"Found {leaf_skills.count()} leaf skills:")
for skill in leaf_skills:
    print(f"  - {skill.name} (parent: {skill.parent.name})")

# Get ancestors of all leaf skills at once
print("\n=== Get Ancestors of All Leaf Skills (One Query) ===")
all_ancestors = leaf_skills.get_ancestors()
print(f"Total unique ancestors: {all_ancestors.count()}")
print("All ancestors:")
for ancestor in all_ancestors.distinct().order_by('level', 'lft'):
    print(f"  Level {ancestor.level}: {ancestor.name}")

# Compare with individual queries
print("\n=== Performance Comparison ===")
print("Individual queries (N queries):")
ancestor_count = 0
for skill in leaf_skills:
    ancestors = skill.get_ancestors()
    ancestor_count += ancestors.count()
    print(f"  {skill.name}: {ancestors.count()} ancestors")

print(f"\nTotal ancestors retrieved individually: {ancestor_count}")
print(f"Unique ancestors from QuerySet: {all_ancestors.distinct().count()}")
print("(TreeQuerySet.get_ancestors() is more efficient for bulk operations)")

# Get ancestors with include_self
print("\n=== Include Self in Results ===")
all_with_self = leaf_skills.get_ancestors(include_self=True)
print(f"Count with include_self=True: {all_with_self.count()}")
print(f"Count without include_self: {all_ancestors.count()}")
print(f"Difference: {all_with_self.count() - all_ancestors.count()} (the leaf skills themselves)")

# Chain with filters
print("\n=== Chaining with Filters ===")
# Get ancestors of Python-related skills only
python_skills = Skills.objects.filter(name__icontains='python').get_ancestors()
print(f"Ancestors of Python-related skills: {python_skills.count()}")
for ancestor in python_skills:
    print(f"  - {ancestor.name}")

# Use with JobPost to find skill hierarchies
print("\n=== Finding Skill Hierarchies for Job Requirements ===")
# Get all skills required by full-time jobs
fulltime_jobs = JobPost.objects.filter(type='Full Time')[:3]
print(f"Analyzing {fulltime_jobs.count()} full-time jobs:")

for job in fulltime_jobs:
    print(f"\n{job.title}:")
    required_skills = job.skills.all()
    print(f"  Direct requirements: {', '.join([s.name for s in required_skills])}")
    
    # Get all ancestors of required skills
    skill_ancestors = required_skills.get_ancestors(include_self=True).distinct()
    print(f"  Complete skill hierarchy ({skill_ancestors.count()} total):")
    
    # Group by level
    for level in range(3):
        level_skills = skill_ancestors.filter(level=level)
        if level_skills.exists():
            print(f"    Level {level}: {', '.join([s.name for s in level_skills])}")

# Practical use case: Permission inheritance
print("\n=== Permission Inheritance Scenario ===")
print("Scenario: Users with Programming permission inherit all sub-skills")
programming = Skills.objects.get(name='Programming')

# Get all descendants
all_skills = programming.get_descendants(include_self=True)
print(f"\nUser with '{programming.name}' permission has access to {all_skills.count()} skills:")
for skill in all_skills.order_by('level', 'lft'):
    indent = "  " * skill.level
    print(f"{indent}- {skill.name}")

# Now check which jobs this user can apply for
eligible_jobs = JobPost.objects.filter(skills__in=all_skills).distinct()
print(f"\nEligible jobs with Programming permission: {eligible_jobs.count()}")
for job in eligible_jobs[:5]:
    print(f"  - {job.title} ({job.location.name})")

]>

# skill_ancestors (for Senior Backend Developer)
<TreeQuerySet [
    <Skills: Programming>,
    <Skills: Python>,
    <Skills: Django>
]>

Insights: TreeQuerySet.get_ancestors() retrieves ancestors for all nodes in one query. Use .distinct() to remove duplicates. Perfect for bulk operations, permission chains, and breadcrumb generation. Chainable with standard QuerySet methods.

Example 2: get_descendants() - Bulk Descendant Retrieval for Category Management

Retrieving descendants of multiple nodes for category management and bulk operations.

from myapp.models import Skills, Location, JobPost
from django.db.models import Count

print("=== Bulk Descendant Retrieval with TreeQuerySet ===\n")

# Get all parent skills (level 1)
print("=== Getting Parent Categories ===")
parent_skills = Skills.objects.filter(level=1)
print(f"Found {parent_skills.count()} parent categories:")
for skill in parent_skills:
    print(f"  - {skill.name} (children: {skill.get_children().count()})")

# Get descendants of all parent skills
print("\n=== Get Descendants of All Parents (One Query) ===")
all_descendants = parent_skills.get_descendants()
print(f"Total descendants: {all_descendants.count()}")
print("Descendants by category:")
for parent in parent_skills:
    parent_descs = all_descendants.filter(lft__gt=parent.lft, rght__lt=parent.rght)
    print(f"  {parent.name}: {parent_descs.count()} descendants")
    for desc in parent_descs:
        print(f"    - {desc.name}")

# Include self for complete subtrees
print("\n=== Include Self for Complete Subtrees ===")
all_with_self = parent_skills.get_descendants(include_self=True)
print(f"Count with include_self=True: {all_with_self.count()}")
print(f"Parent skills + descendants: {parent_skills.count()} + {all_descendants.count()} = {all_with_self.count()}")

# Chain with additional filters
print("\n=== Chaining with Filters ===")
# Get only leaf nodes from descendants
leaf_descendants = all_descendants.filter(rght=models.F('lft') + 1)
print(f"Leaf nodes among descendants: {leaf_descendants.count()}")
for leaf in leaf_descendants:
    print(f"  - {leaf.name}")

# Location tree example
print("\n=== Location Tree Descendant Analysis ===")
# Get all countries
countries = Location.objects.filter(level=1)
print(f"Found {countries.count()} countries:")

for country in countries:
    print(f"\n{country.name}:")
    # Get all locations in this country
    country_locs = Location.objects.filter(
        lft__gte=country.lft, 
        rght__lte=country.rght
    ).exclude(id=country.id)
    
    states = country_locs.filter(level=2)
    cities = country_locs.filter(level=3)
    
    print(f"  States/Provinces: {states.count()}")
    print(f"  Cities: {cities.count()}")
    print(f"  Total locations: {country_locs.count()}")

# Bulk descendants for multiple roots
print("\n=== Multiple Root Descendants ===")
# Get descendants of specific skills
selected_skills = Skills.objects.filter(name__in=['Python', 'JavaScript'])
print(f"Selected skills: {', '.join([s.name for s in selected_skills])}")

selected_descendants = selected_skills.get_descendants(include_self=True)
print(f"Total skills in selected categories: {selected_descendants.count()}")
for skill in selected_descendants.order_by('tree_id', 'lft'):
    indent = "  " * (skill.level - 1)
    print(f"{indent}- {skill.name}")

# Practical use case: Job filtering by skill categories
print("\n=== Job Filtering by Skill Categories ===")
print("Find all jobs requiring Python or its sub-skills:")
python = Skills.objects.get(name='Python')
python_tree = Skills.objects.filter(
    lft__gte=python.lft,
    rght__lte=python.rght
)

python_jobs = JobPost.objects.filter(skills__in=python_tree).distinct()
print(f"Jobs requiring Python skills: {python_jobs.count()}")
for job in python_jobs[:5]:
    job_skills = job.skills.filter(id__in=python_tree)
    print(f"  - {job.title}: {', '.join([s.name for s in job_skills])}")

# Annotate with descendant counts
print("\n=== Annotating Categories with Job Counts ===")
# For each parent skill, count jobs requiring it or its descendants
for parent in parent_skills:
    # Get all skills in this category
    category_skills = Skills.objects.filter(
        lft__gte=parent.lft,
        rght__lte=parent.rght
    )
    
    # Count jobs
    job_count = JobPost.objects.filter(
        skills__in=category_skills
    ).distinct().count()
    
    print(f"{parent.name}: {job_count} jobs ({category_skills.count()} skills in category)")

# Bulk update scenario
print("\n=== Bulk Operations on Descendants ===")
print("Scenario: Get all descendants for bulk updates")
programming = Skills.objects.get(name='Programming')
all_programming_skills = programming.get_descendants(include_self=True)

print(f"\nAll skills in Programming tree: {all_programming_skills.count()}")
print("These could be bulk updated with:")
print("  - Add 'is_tech_skill=True' flag")
print("  - Update 'category=Programming' field")
print("  - Apply bulk permission changes")
print(f"  - affected_count = all_programming_skills.update(is_tech_skill=True)")

# Complex filtering with descendants
print("\n=== Complex Queries with Descendants ===")
# Get all locations with jobs, then get their descendants
locations_with_jobs = Location.objects.filter(
    jobpost__isnull=False
).distinct()

print(f"Locations with jobs: {locations_with_jobs.count()}")
for loc in locations_with_jobs[:3]:
    print(f"  - {loc.name}: {loc.jobpost_set.count()} jobs")

# Get descendants of these locations
descendant_locations = locations_with_jobs.get_descendants()
print(f"\nDescendant locations: {descendant_locations.count()}")
print("(Child locations that might also have jobs or be relevant for filtering)")

Example 3: get_cached_trees() - Optimized Tree Rendering with Caching

Building cached tree structures for efficient template rendering without N+1 query problems.

from myapp.models import Skills, Location
from django.db import connection, reset_queries
from django.conf import settings

# Enable query logging
settings.DEBUG = True
reset_queries()

print("=== Cached Tree Rendering (get_cached_trees) ===\n")

# Method 1: Without caching (N+1 problem)
print("=== Method 1: Without Caching (N+1 Problem) ===")
reset_queries()

all_skills = Skills.objects.all()
print("Rendering tree without caching:")

def render_tree_uncached(nodes, level=0):
    """Recursively render tree - causes N+1 queries"""
    for node in nodes.filter(level=level):
        print("  " * level + f"- {node.name}")
        # This causes a query for each node
        render_tree_uncached(nodes, level + 1)

# This would cause many queries, so we'll skip actual rendering
print(f"Total nodes: {all_skills.count()}")
print(f"Queries made: {len(connection.queries)}")
print("Problem: Each node access would trigger separate query for children")

# Method 2: Using get_cached_trees (Optimized)
print("\n=== Method 2: Using get_cached_trees (Optimized) ===")
reset_queries()

cached_trees = Skills.objects.all().get_cached_trees()
print(f"Query count after get_cached_trees: {len(connection.queries)}")
print(f"Returned: {type(cached_trees)} with {len(cached_trees)} root(s)")

print("\nRendering cached tree:")
def render_cached_tree(nodes, level=0):
    """Render tree from cached structure - no additional queries"""
    for node in nodes:
        print("  " * level + f"- {node.name}")
        # Access children from cache - no query!
        if hasattr(node, 'get_children'):
            children = node.get_children()
            if children:
                render_cached_tree(children, level + 1)

render_cached_tree(cached_trees)
print(f"\nTotal queries for entire tree: {len(connection.queries)}")
print("Benefit: Only 1-2 queries regardless of tree depth!")

# Location tree with caching
print("\n=== Location Tree with Caching ===")
reset_queries()

location_trees = Location.objects.all().get_cached_trees()
print(f"Location roots: {len(location_trees)}")
print(f"Queries: {len(connection.queries)}")

print("\nComplete location hierarchy:")
for continent in location_trees:
    print(f"{continent.name}")
    
    # Countries
    if hasattr(continent, 'get_children'):
        for country in continent.get_children():
            print(f"  └─ {country.name}")
            
            # States
            if hasattr(country, 'get_children'):
                for state in country.get_children():
                    print(f"      └─ {state.name}")
                    
                    # Cities
                    if hasattr(state, 'get_children'):
                        for city in state.get_children():
                            print(f"          └─ {city.name}")

print(f"\nTotal queries: {len(connection.queries)}")

# Filtered cached trees
print("\n=== Filtered Cached Trees ===")
reset_queries()

# Get cached trees for only certain nodes
python_branch = Skills.objects.filter(
    lft__gte=Skills.objects.get(name='Python').lft,
    rght__lte=Skills.objects.get(name='Python').rght
).get_cached_trees()

print(f"Python branch cached: {len(python_branch)} root(s)")
for root in python_branch:
    print(f"{root.name}")
    if hasattr(root, 'get_children'):
        for child in root.get_children():
            print(f"  - {child.name}")

print(f"Queries: {len(connection.queries)}")

# Performance comparison
print("\n=== Performance Comparison ===")
print("Scenario: Rendering tree with 10 nodes, depth 3")
print("\nWithout caching:")
print("  - Query for root nodes: 1 query")
print("  - Query for each node's children: 10 queries")
print("  - Total: ~11+ queries")

print("\nWith get_cached_trees():")
print("  - Initial fetch: 1-2 queries")
print("  - Access children: 0 queries (cached)")
print("  - Total: 1-2 queries")

print("\nSpeedup: 5-10x faster for typical trees")

# Template rendering example
print("\n=== Template Rendering Example ===")
print("In Django template:")
print("""
{% load mptt_tags %}



    
    {% for skill in all_skills %}
        {% if skill.is_root_node %}
        
  • {{ skill.name }}
            
      
            {% for child in skill.get_children %}
                
    • {{ child.name }}
      •   
            {% endfor %}
            
    
        
    • 
        {% endif %}
    {% endfor %}




{% recursetree cached_trees %}
    
  • 
        {{ node.name }}
        {% if not node.is_leaf_node %}
            
      
                {{ children }}
            
    
        {% endif %}
    
    • 
{% endrecursetree %}
""")

# Practical use case: Navigation menu
print("\n=== Building Navigation Menu ===")
reset_queries()

# Get cached tree for navigation
nav_skills = Skills.objects.filter(level__lte=1).get_cached_trees()
print(f"Navigation menu cached: {len(nav_skills)} sections")

print("\nNavigation structure:")
for root in nav_skills:
    print(f"📁 {root.name}")
    if hasattr(root, 'get_children'):
        for category in root.get_children():
            child_count = category.get_children().count() if hasattr(category, 'get_children') else 0
            print(f"  📄 {category.name} ({child_count} items)")

print(f"\nQueries for navigation: {len(connection.queries)}")

# Advanced: Custom tree builder
print("\n=== Custom Tree Structure Builder ===")
def build_tree_dict(nodes):
    """Build nested dictionary from cached trees"""
    tree = []
    for node in nodes:
        node_dict = {
            'id': node.id,
            'name': node.name,
            'level': node.level,
            'children': []
        }
        if hasattr(node, 'get_children'):
            children = node.get_children()
            if children:
                node_dict['children'] = build_tree_dict(children)
        tree.append(node_dict)
    return tree

reset_queries()
cached = Skills.objects.all().get_cached_trees()
tree_dict = build_tree_dict(cached)

print(f"Built tree dictionary with {len(tree_dict)} roots")
print(f"Queries: {len(connection.queries)}")
print("\nSample structure:")
import json
print(json.dumps(tree_dict[0], indent=2))

# Memory efficiency note
print("\n=== Memory Considerations ===")
all_skills_count = Skills.objects.count()
print(f"Total skills: {all_skills_count}")
print(f"Memory usage: ~{all_skills_count * 1} KB (approximate)")
print("Cached trees load all nodes into memory at once")
print("Best for small-medium trees (<1000 nodes)")
print("For large trees, consider pagination or lazy loading")

    Example 4: Chaining TreeQuerySet with Standard Django QuerySet Methods

    Combining tree-specific methods with Django's QuerySet API for complex filtering and aggregation.

    from myapp.models import Skills, JobPost, Location
from django.db.models import Count, Q, F, Avg, Max
from django.db.models.functions import Length

print("=== Chaining TreeQuerySet with Django ORM ===\n")

# Example 1: Filter + get_ancestors
print("=== Filtering Before get_ancestors() ===")
# Find ancestors of skills with 'a' in name
skills_with_a = Skills.objects.filter(name__icontains='a')
print(f"Skills containing 'a': {skills_with_a.count()}")
for skill in skills_with_a:
    print(f"  - {skill.name}")

ancestors_of_a = skills_with_a.get_ancestors().distinct()
print(f"\nUnique ancestors: {ancestors_of_a.count()}")
for ancestor in ancestors_of_a.order_by('level', 'name'):
    print(f"  Level {ancestor.level}: {ancestor.name}")

# Example 2: get_descendants + filter
print("\n=== get_descendants() + Additional Filtering ===")
programming = Skills.objects.get(name='Programming')
all_descendants = programming.get_descendants()

# Filter descendants further
python_related = all_descendants.filter(name__icontains='python')
print(f"Python-related descendants: {python_related.count()}")
for skill in python_related:
    print(f"  - {skill.name} (level {skill.level})")

# Filter by level
level_2_descendants = all_descendants.filter(level=2)
print(f"\nLevel 2 descendants: {level_2_descendants.count()}")
for skill in level_2_descendants:
    print(f"  - {skill.name}")

# Example 3: Annotate with counts
print("\n=== Annotating TreeQuerySet with Counts ===")
# Count jobs for each skill category
parent_skills = Skills.objects.filter(level=1).annotate(
    job_count=Count('job_posts', distinct=True),
    descendant_skills=Count('id')  # Will show 1, need custom logic
)

print("Skills with job counts:")
for skill in parent_skills:
    # Get descendants and count their jobs too
    all_in_category = Skills.objects.filter(
        lft__gte=skill.lft,
        rght__lte=skill.rght
    )
    total_jobs = JobPost.objects.filter(
        skills__in=all_in_category
    ).distinct().count()
    
    print(f"  {skill.name}:")
    print(f"    Direct jobs: {skill.job_count}")
    print(f"    Total jobs (incl. descendants): {total_jobs}")
    print(f"    Skills in category: {all_in_category.count()}")

# Example 4: Complex Q objects with tree queries
print("\n=== Complex Filtering with Q Objects ===")
# Find skills that are either:
# 1. Root nodes OR
# 2. Have 'Script' in name OR
# 3. Are descendants of Java

java = Skills.objects.get(name='Java')
java_descendants = java.get_descendants(include_self=True)

complex_filter = Skills.objects.filter(
    Q(level=0) |  # Root nodes
    Q(name__icontains='script') |  # Name contains 'script'
    Q(id__in=java_descendants)  # Java family
).distinct()

print(f"Skills matching complex filter: {complex_filter.count()}")
for skill in complex_filter.order_by('tree_id', 'lft'):
    reasons = []
    if skill.level == 0:
        reasons.append("ROOT")
    if 'script' in skill.name.lower():
        reasons.append("HAS 'SCRIPT'")
    if skill.id in [j.id for j in java_descendants]:
        reasons.append("JAVA FAMILY")
    
    print(f"  - {skill.name} [{', '.join(reasons)}]")

# Example 5: select_related and prefetch_related
print("\n=== Optimizing with select_related ===")
from django.db import connection, reset_queries
from django.conf import settings
settings.DEBUG = True

# Get jobs with location tree
reset_queries()
jobs_with_locations = JobPost.objects.all().select_related(
    'location',
    'location__parent',
    'location__parent__parent'
)[:5]

print("Jobs with location hierarchy (select_related):")
for job in jobs_with_locations:
    loc_path = []
    current = job.location
    while current:
        loc_path.insert(0, current.name)
        current = current.parent
    
    print(f"  {job.title}: {' > '.join(loc_path)}")

print(f"Queries used: {len(connection.queries)}")

# Example 6: prefetch_related for M2M
print("\n=== Prefetch Skills with TreeQuerySet ===")
reset_queries()

jobs = JobPost.objects.prefetch_related('skills')[:3]
print("Jobs with prefetched skills:")
for job in jobs:
    skills = job.skills.all()  # No additional query
    print(f"\n  {job.title}:")
    print(f"    Skills: {', '.join([s.name for s in skills])}")
    
    # Get ancestors of job skills
    if skills.exists():
        ancestors = skills.get_ancestors().distinct()
        print(f"    Skill categories: {', '.join([a.name for a in ancestors.filter(level=0)])}")

print(f"\nTotal queries: {len(connection.queries)}")

# Example 7: Aggregation with tree queries
print("\n=== Aggregation on Tree Structures ===")
# Average job count per skill category
stats = Skills.objects.filter(level=1).annotate(
    total_jobs=Count('job_posts', distinct=True)
).aggregate(
    avg_jobs=Avg('total_jobs'),
    max_jobs=Max('total_jobs'),
    total=Count('id')
)

print(f"Skill category statistics:")
print(f"  Total categories: {stats['total']}")
print(f"  Average jobs per category: {stats['avg_jobs']:.1f}")
print(f"  Max jobs in one category: {stats['max_jobs']}")

# Example 8: Exclude with tree queries
print("\n=== Excluding Nodes with Tree Awareness ===")
# Get all skills except Python branch
python = Skills.objects.get(name='Python')
non_python = Skills.objects.exclude(
    lft__gte=python.lft,
    rght__lte=python.rght
)

print(f"Skills excluding Python branch: {non_python.count()}")
for skill in non_python.order_by('lft'):
    indent = "  " * skill.level
    print(f"{indent}- {skill.name}")

# Example 9: Order by with tree structure
print("\n=== Custom Ordering with Tree Queries ===")
# Get leaf skills ordered by name length
leaf_skills = Skills.objects.filter(
    rght=F('lft') + 1
).annotate(
    name_length=Length('name')
).order_by('-name_length')

print("Leaf skills by name length (longest first):")
for skill in leaf_skills:
    path = ' > '.join([a.name for a in skill.get_ancestors(include_self=True)])
    print(f"  {skill.name} ({len(skill.name)} chars): {path}")

# Example 10: Combining multiple tree operations
print("\n=== Complex Multi-Step Tree Query ===")
print("Find: Leaf skills from Python category that have jobs in California")

# Step 1: Get Python descendants
python_skills = Skills.objects.filter(
    lft__gte=python.lft,
    rght__lte=python.rght
)

# Step 2: Filter to only leaves
python_leaves = python_skills.filter(rght=F('lft') + 1)

# Step 3: Get California locations
california = Location.objects.get(name='California')
ca_locations = Location.objects.filter(
    lft__gte=california.lft,
    rght__lte=california.rght
)

# Step 4: Find jobs matching all criteria
matching_jobs = JobPost.objects.filter(
    skills__in=python_leaves,
    location__in=ca_locations
).distinct()

print(f"Found {matching_jobs.count()} matching jobs:")
for job in matching_jobs:
    job_skills = job.skills.filter(id__in=python_leaves)
    print(f"  - {job.title}")
    print(f"      Location: {job.location.name}")
    print(f"      Skills: {', '.join([s.name for s in job_skills])}")

# Show the power of chaining
print("\n=== QuerySet Chaining Power ===")
chained = Skills.objects.filter(
    level__gte=1  # Not root
).exclude(
    name__icontains='spring'  # Not Spring-related
).get_ancestors(  # Get their ancestors
    include_self=False
).distinct(  # Remove duplicates
).order_by('lft')  # Tree order

print(f"Result of complex chain: {chained.count()} skills")
for skill in chained:
    print(f"  - {skill.name} (level {skill.level})")
