    Example 5: Creating Custom Managers with as_manager() and Custom TreeQuerySet

    Extending TreeQuerySet with custom methods and creating reusable managers for common queries.

    from mptt.querysets import TreeQuerySet
from mptt.models import MPTTModel, TreeForeignKey
from django.db import models

print("=== Custom Managers from TreeQuerySet ===\n")

# Define custom TreeQuerySet with business logic
print("=== Step 1: Define Custom TreeQuerySet ===")
print("""
class SkillQuerySet(TreeQuerySet):
    '''Custom QuerySet with domain-specific methods'''
    
    def active_only(self):
        '''Return only active skills'''
        return self.filter(is_active=True)
    
    def with_jobs(self):
        '''Return skills that have associated jobs'''
        return self.filter(job_posts__isnull=False).distinct()
    
    def popular(self, min_jobs=3):
        '''Return skills with at least min_jobs'''
        from django.db.models import Count
        return self.annotate(
            job_count=Count('job_posts', distinct=True)
        ).filter(job_count__gte=min_jobs)
    
    def by_category(self, category_name):
        '''Return all skills in a category (including descendants)'''
        try:
            category = self.get(name=category_name)
            return self.filter(
                lft__gte=category.lft,
                rght__lte=category.rght
            )
        except self.model.DoesNotExist:
            return self.none()
    
    def leaf_skills(self):
        '''Return only leaf nodes (actual skills, not categories)'''
        return self.filter(rght=models.F('lft') + 1)
    
    def with_full_path(self):
        '''Annotate with full category path'''
        # This is conceptual - actual implementation would cache paths
        return self

# Model using custom manager
class Skill(MPTTModel):
    name = models.CharField(max_length=200)
    is_active = models.BooleanField(default=True)
    parent = TreeForeignKey('self', on_delete=models.CASCADE,
                           null=True, blank=True, 
                           related_name='children')
    
    # Use custom QuerySet as manager
    objects = SkillQuerySet.as_manager()
    
    class MPTTMeta:
        order_insertion_by = ['name']
""")

# Demonstrate usage (using Skills model as proxy)
print("\n=== Step 2: Using Custom Manager Methods ===")
from myapp.models import Skills, JobPost

# Method 1: with_jobs()
print("Skills with jobs (with_jobs method):")
skills_with_jobs = Skills.objects.filter(job_posts__isnull=False).distinct()
print(f"Count: {skills_with_jobs.count()}")
for skill in skills_with_jobs[:5]:
    job_count = skill.job_posts.count()
    print(f"  - {skill.name}: {job_count} jobs")

# Method 2: popular(min_jobs)
print("\n=== Popular Skills (3+ jobs) ===")
from django.db.models import Count

popular_skills = Skills.objects.annotate(
    job_count=Count('job_posts', distinct=True)
).filter(job_count__gte=3)

print(f"Skills with 3+ jobs: {popular_skills.count()}")
for skill in popular_skills.order_by('-job_count'):
    print(f"  - {skill.name}: {skill.job_count} jobs")

# Method 3: by_category()
print("\n=== Skills by Category ===")
python_category = Skills.objects.get(name='Python')
python_skills = Skills.objects.filter(
    lft__gte=python_category.lft,
    rght__lte=python_category.rght
)

print(f"All skills in Python category: {python_skills.count()}")
for skill in python_skills.order_by('level', 'lft'):
    indent = "  " * skill.level
    print(f"{indent}- {skill.name} (level {skill.level})")

# Method 4: leaf_skills()
print("\n=== Leaf Skills Only ===")
from django.db.models import F

leaf_skills = Skills.objects.filter(rght=F('lft') + 1)
print(f"Total leaf skills: {leaf_skills.count()}")
for skill in leaf_skills:
    parent_chain = ' > '.join([a.name for a in skill.get_ancestors()])
    print(f"  - {skill.name} (parent: {parent_chain})")

# Chaining custom methods
print("\n=== Chaining Custom Methods ===")
print("Popular leaf skills with jobs:")

# Simulate chaining: leaf_skills().with_jobs().popular()
popular_leaves = Skills.objects.filter(
    rght=F('lft') + 1  # leaf_skills()
).filter(
    job_posts__isnull=False  # with_jobs()
).annotate(
    job_count=Count('job_posts', distinct=True)
).filter(
    job_count__gte=2  # popular(min_jobs=2)
).distinct()

print(f"Count: {popular_leaves.count()}")
for skill in popular_leaves.order_by('-job_count'):
    print(f"  - {skill.name}: {skill.job_count} jobs")

# Combining with tree methods
print("\n=== Combining Custom and Tree Methods ===")
print("Get ancestors of popular skills:")

popular = Skills.objects.annotate(
    job_count=Count('job_posts', distinct=True)
).filter(job_count__gte=3)

popular_ancestors = popular.get_ancestors().distinct()
print(f"Ancestors of popular skills: {popular_ancestors.count()}")
for ancestor in popular_ancestors.order_by('level', 'lft'):
    print(f"  Level {ancestor.level}: {ancestor.name}")

# Real-world example: Skill recommendation system
print("\n=== Real-World Example: Skill Recommendations ===")
print("Recommend related skills based on job requirements")

# Get a sample job
job = JobPost.objects.filter(skills__isnull=False).first()
print(f"\nJob: {job.title}")
print(f"Location: {job.location.name}")

# Required skills
required = job.skills.all()
print(f"Required skills: {', '.join([s.name for s in required])}")

# Get all skills in same categories
related_categories = required.get_ancestors(include_self=True).filter(level__lte=1)
print(f"\nRelated categories: {', '.join([c.name for c in related_categories.distinct()])}")

# Get all skills in those categories
recommended = Skills.objects.none()
for category in related_categories:
    category_skills = Skills.objects.filter(
        lft__gte=category.lft,
        rght__lte=category.rght
    )
    recommended = recommended | category_skills

# Exclude already required
recommended = recommended.exclude(
    id__in=required
).filter(
    rght=F('lft') + 1  # Only leaves
).distinct()

print(f"Recommended skills: {recommended.count()}")
for skill in recommended[:5]:
    # Count how many jobs need this skill
    skill_jobs = skill.job_posts.count()
    print(f"  - {skill.name} (used in {skill_jobs} jobs)")

# Advanced: Multi-database support
print("\n=== Multi-Database Custom Manager ===")
print("Example: Separate read/write databases")
print("""
class SkillQuerySet(TreeQuerySet):
    def using_read_db(self):
        '''Use read replica'''
        return self.using('read_replica')
    
    def using_write_db(self):
        '''Use write database'''
        return self.using('default')

# Usage:
# read_skills = Skills.objects.using_read_db().all()
# write_skills = Skills.objects.using_write_db().create(name='New')
""")

# Manager inheritance
print("\n=== Manager Inheritance Pattern ===")
print("""
# Base QuerySet with common methods
class BaseTreeQuerySet(TreeQuerySet):
    def active(self):
        return self.filter(is_active=True)
    
    def created_after(self, date):
        return self.filter(created_at__gte=date)

# Specialized QuerySets
class SkillQuerySet(BaseTreeQuerySet):
    def with_jobs(self):
        return self.filter(job_posts__isnull=False)

class LocationQuerySet(BaseTreeQuerySet):
    def in_country(self, country):
        return self.filter(country=country)

# Models use specialized managers
class Skill(MPTTModel):
    objects = SkillQuerySet.as_manager()

class Location(MPTTModel):
    objects = LocationQuerySet.as_manager()
""")

# Performance note
print("\n=== Performance Benefits ===")
print("Custom managers provide:")
print("  ✓ Reusable business logic")
print("  ✓ Consistent querying patterns")
print("  ✓ Reduced code duplication")
print("  ✓ Easier testing and maintenance")
print("  ✓ Chainable with tree methods")
print("  ✓ Type hints and IDE autocomplete")

# Summary
print("\n=== Summary: as_manager() Benefits ===")
print("1. Encapsulate complex queries in named methods")
print("2. Make code more readable and maintainable")
print("3. Share common logic across views/serializers")
print("4. Combine domain logic with tree operations")
print("5. Easy to test individual query methods")
print("6. Supports method chaining")
print("7. Works seamlessly with Django admin and forms")

class SkillQuerySet(TreeQuerySet):
    '''Custom QuerySet with domain-specific methods'''
    
    def active_only(self):
        '''Return only active skills'''
        return self.filter(is_active=True)
    
    def with_jobs(self):
        '''Return skills that have associated jobs'''
        return self.filter(job_posts__isnull=False).distinct()

        '''Return skills with at least min_jobs'''
        from django.db.models import Count
        return self.annotate(
            job_count=Count('job_posts', distinct=True)
        ).filter(job_count__gte=min_jobs)
    
    def by_category(self, category_name):
        '''Return all skills in a category (including descendants)'''
        try:
            category = self.get(name=category_name)
            return self.filter(
                lft__gte=category.lft,
                rght__lte=category.rght
            )
        except self.model.DoesNotExist:
            return self.none()
    
    def leaf_skills(self):
        '''Return only leaf nodes (actual skills, not categories)'''
        return self.filter(rght=models.F('lft') + 1)
    
    def with_full_path(self):
        '''Annotate with full category path'''
        # This is conceptual - actual implementation would cache paths
        return self

class Location(MPTTModel):
    objects = LocationQuerySet.as_manager()

    🛠️ mptt.utils - Utility Functions for Tree Operations

    The mptt.utils module provides a collection of utility functions designed to simplify common tree operations and enhance tree traversal capabilities. These helper functions handle tasks like creating drilldown trees, caching tree structures, and iterating over tree items with context awareness. They are particularly useful for template rendering, tree visualization, and building navigation components.

    The utilities in this module complement the core MPTT functionality by providing higher-level abstractions that solve common use cases. They handle the complexity of tree traversal, level management, and ancestor tracking, making it easier to build sophisticated tree-based features without writing custom traversal logic.

    Module Components

    The mptt.utils module contains standalone utility functions:

    • drilldown_tree_for_node() - Creates focused tree view with ancestors and children
    • get_cached_trees() - Builds cached tree structures for efficient rendering
    • previous_current_next() - Iterator providing context triples
    • tree_item_iterator() - Enhanced iteration with level and ancestor information

    Utility Functions

    Overview

    mptt.utils functions are standalone helpers that operate on tree nodes and querysets. Unlike methods on models or managers, these are pure functions that can be imported and used independently, providing flexibility in how you structure your code.

    Syntax

    from mptt.utils import (
    drilldown_tree_for_node,
    get_cached_trees,
    previous_current_next,
    tree_item_iterator
)

# drilldown_tree_for_node() - Focused tree view
drilldown = drilldown_tree_for_node(node)

# get_cached_trees() - Pre-load tree structure
cached_roots = get_cached_trees(queryset)

# previous_current_next() - Context iterator
for prev, current, next in previous_current_next(items):
    pass

# tree_item_iterator() - Enhanced tree iteration
for item, structure in tree_item_iterator(nodes):
    pass

    Parameters

    Note: Each utility function has its own specific parameters. See individual function documentation below for detailed parameter descriptions:

    • drilldown_tree_for_node() - node, rel_cls, rel_field, count_attr, cumulative, all_descendants
    • get_cached_trees() - queryset
    • previous_current_next() - items
    • tree_item_iterator() - items

    Attributes

    These are standalone functions and do not have attributes. They operate on nodes and querysets passed as arguments.

    Methods

    The following utility functions are available in mptt.utils:

    drilldown_tree_for_node()

    drilldown_tree_for_node() creates a focused view of a tree centered around a specific node. It returns the node's ancestors, the node itself, and its immediate children (or all descendants), all in tree order. This is perfect for building breadcrumb navigation, hierarchical menus with context, and focused tree views where you want to show a path to a specific node along with its immediate children.

    Common Use Cases:

    • Breadcrumb navigation with sibling context
    • Category browser showing path and subcategories
    • Organizational chart focused on a specific person
    • File system explorer showing current folder context
    • Menu systems with highlighted active path
    Syntax
    from mptt.utils import drilldown_tree_for_node

# Basic usage - ancestors + node + immediate children
drilldown = drilldown_tree_for_node(node)

# With related counts
drilldown = drilldown_tree_for_node(
    node,
    rel_cls=JobPost,
    rel_field='location',
    count_attr='job_count'
)

# All descendants instead of just children
drilldown = drilldown_tree_for_node(
    node,
    all_descendants=True
)

# Cumulative counts (include descendant counts)
drilldown = drilldown_tree_for_node(
    node,
    rel_cls=JobPost,
    rel_field='skills',
    count_attr='total_jobs',
    cumulative=True
)
    Parameters
    node (MPTTModel instance, required): The node to create the drilldown tree for. Must be an instance of an MPTT model.
    rel_cls (Model class, optional): A Django model class that has a foreign key relation to the node's class. Used for adding related item counts to children.
    rel_field (str, optional): The name of the field in rel_cls that holds the foreign key to the node's class. Required if rel_cls is specified.
    count_attr (str, optional): The name of an attribute to add to each child node containing the count of related rel_cls instances. Required if rel_cls is specified.
    cumulative (bool, default=False): If True, counts include the node and all its descendants. If False, counts only direct relations to the node.
    all_descendants (bool, default=False): If True, returns all descendants of the node. If False, returns only immediate children.
    Return Value

    Returns: QuerySet of nodes in tree order containing ancestors, the node itself, and children/descendants

    Return Type: QuerySet (TreeQuerySet)

    get_cached_trees()

    get_cached_trees() builds cached tree structures from a queryset, pre-loading all parent-child relationships into memory. This eliminates N+1 query problems when rendering complete trees, making it ideal for template rendering, JSON serialization, and any scenario where you need to traverse multiple levels of a tree without triggering additional database queries.

    Common Use Cases:

    • Rendering complete navigation menus
    • Building JSON API responses with nested structures
    • Template-based tree rendering with recursive includes
    • Category trees for e-commerce sites
    • Organizational charts and hierarchical displays
    Syntax
    from mptt.utils import get_cached_trees

# Cache all nodes
all_nodes = YourModel.objects.all()
cached_roots = get_cached_trees(all_nodes)

# Cache filtered nodes
active_nodes = YourModel.objects.filter(is_active=True)
cached_roots = get_cached_trees(active_nodes)

# Common pattern with queryset
cached_roots = get_cached_trees(
    YourModel.objects.filter(level__lte=2).order_by('tree_id', 'lft')
)
    Parameters
    queryset (QuerySet or list, required): A queryset or list containing all nodes to cache. Must be ordered by tree_id and lft (ascending). Nodes not in this queryset won't be accessible through the cache.
    Return Value

    Returns: List of root nodes with all descendants pre-cached in memory. Each root node has its children accessible via get_children() without additional queries.

    Return Type: list

    Important: The queryset MUST be ordered by tree_id and lft ascending for correct results. Returns one node per tree root.

    Aliases

    This function is also available through the following aliases:

    • mptt.templatetags.mptt_tag.cache_tree_children - Template tag for use in Django templates. Use for recursive rendering in templates.
    • mptt.querysets.TreeQuerySet.get_cached_trees - Chainable queryset method. Useful for chaining with queries: Node.objects.filter(**kwargs).get_cached_trees()

    Template Usage Example:

    {% load mptt_tags %}

{% cache_tree_children nodes %}
{% recursetree nodes %}
    <li>
        {{ node.name }}
        {% if not node.is_leaf_node %}
            <ul class="children">{{ children }}</ul>
        {% endif %}
    </li>
{% endrecursetree %}

    previous_current_next()

    previous_current_next() creates an iterator that yields (previous, current, next) triples for any iterable. This is useful for template rendering where you need to know what comes before and after the current item, such as for navigation links, visual indicators, or conditional formatting based on position.

    Common Use Cases:

    • Adding "first" and "last" classes in templates
    • Building pagination with prev/next links
    • Visual separators between items (not after last)
    • Context-aware formatting (different style for middle items)
    • Navigation breadcrumbs with arrows
    Syntax
    from mptt.utils import previous_current_next

# Basic usage
items = ['A', 'B', 'C']
for prev, current, next_item in previous_current_next(items):
    print(f"Previous: {prev}, Current: {current}, Next: {next_item}")

# With tree nodes
nodes = YourModel.objects.all()
for prev_node, current_node, next_node in previous_current_next(nodes):
    if prev_node is None:
        print(f"{current_node.name} is first")
    elif next_node is None:
        print(f"{current_node.name} is last")
    else:
        print(f"{current_node.name} is between {prev_node.name} and {next_node.name}")
    Parameters
    items (iterable, required): Any iterable (list, queryset, etc.). The function will iterate through and provide context triples.
    Return Value

    Returns: Generator yielding (previous, current, next) tuples. First item has previous=None, last item has next=None.

    Return Type: generator

    tree_item_iterator()

    tree_item_iterator() creates an enhanced iterator for tree items that provides structural information about each node's position in the tree. It yields (item, info_dict) tuples where info_dict contains flags for new levels, closed levels, and optionally ancestor chains. This is essential for rendering trees with proper indentation, level indicators, and hierarchical context.

    Common Use Cases:

    • Rendering indented tree structures with proper nesting
    • Adding open/close tags for nested HTML lists
    • Building tree tables with rowspan for levels
    • Visual tree with connecting lines
    • Breadcrumb generation during iteration
    Syntax
    from mptt.utils import tree_item_iterator

# Basic usage
nodes = YourModel.objects.all()
for node, info in tree_item_iterator(nodes):
    if info['new_level']:
        print(f"  Starting new level")
    print(f"{'  ' * node.level}{node.name}")
    for closed in info['closed_levels']:
        print(f"  Closing level {closed}")

# With ancestors
for node, info in tree_item_iterator(nodes, ancestors=True):
    ancestor_names = [a for a in info['ancestors']]
    path = ' > '.join(ancestor_names + [str(node)])
    print(path)

# Custom callback for ancestor representation
for node, info in tree_item_iterator(nodes, ancestors=True, callback=lambda n: n.name):
    print(f"Ancestors: {' > '.join(info['ancestors'])}")
    Parameters
    items (iterable, required): List or queryset of tree nodes to iterate over. Should be in tree order (ordered by tree_id, lft).
    ancestors (bool, default=False): If True, includes 'ancestors' key in info dict with list of ancestor representations in descending order (root first).
    callback (callable, default=str): Function to convert nodes to strings for ancestor list. Receives node instance, returns string representation.
    Return Value

    Returns: Generator yielding (node, info_dict) tuples

    Return Type: generator

    info_dict keys:

    • 'new_level' (bool): True if this node starts a new level
    • 'closed_levels' (list): List of level numbers that end after this node
    • 'ancestors' (list, optional): List of ancestor representations if ancestors=True

    Examples

    Example 1: drilldown_tree_for_node() - Creating Focused Tree Views with Context

    Building focused tree views that show a node's position with ancestors and children.

    from mptt.utils import drilldown_tree_for_node
from myapp.models import Skills, Location, JobPost

print("=== Drilldown Tree for Node ===\n")

# Example 1: Basic drilldown (ancestors + node + children)
print("=== Basic Drilldown for Django Skill ===")
django_skill = Skills.objects.get(name='Django')
drilldown = drilldown_tree_for_node(django_skill)

print(f"Drilldown tree for: {django_skill.name}")
print(f"Total nodes in drilldown: {drilldown.count()}")
print("\nDrilldown contents:")
for node in drilldown:
    indent = "  " * node.level
    marker = " ← TARGET" if node == django_skill else ""
    node_type = "ANCESTOR" if node.is_ancestor_of(django_skill) else \
                 "CHILD" if django_skill.is_ancestor_of(node) else "SELF"
    print(f"{indent}{node.name} [{node_type}]{marker}")

# Example 2: Drilldown with all descendants
print("\n=== Drilldown with All Descendants ===")
python = Skills.objects.get(name='Python')
full_drilldown = drilldown_tree_for_node(python, all_descendants=True)

print(f"Drilldown for: {python.name} (all_descendants=True)")
print(f"Total nodes: {full_drilldown.count()}")
for node in full_drilldown:
    indent = "  " * node.level
    marker = " ← TARGET" if node == python else ""
    print(f"{indent}{node.name}{marker}")

# Example 3: Drilldown with related counts
print("\n=== Drilldown with Job Counts ===")
california = Location.objects.get(name='California')
drilldown_with_counts = drilldown_tree_for_node(
    california,
    rel_cls=JobPost,
    rel_field='location',
    count_attr='job_count'
)

print(f"Drilldown for: {california.name}")
print("With job counts (direct only):\n")
for node in drilldown_with_counts:
    indent = "  " * node.level
    marker = " ← TARGET" if node == california else ""
    count = getattr(node, 'job_count', 0)
    print(f"{indent}{node.name}: {count} jobs{marker}")

# Example 4: Cumulative counts
print("\n=== Drilldown with Cumulative Counts ===")
usa = Location.objects.get(name='USA')
cumulative_drilldown = drilldown_tree_for_node(
    usa,
    rel_cls=JobPost,
    rel_field='location',
    count_attr='total_jobs',
    cumulative=True
)

print(f"Drilldown for: {usa.name}")
print("With cumulative job counts (including descendants):\n")
for node in cumulative_drilldown:
    indent = "  " * node.level
    marker = " ← TARGET" if node == usa else ""
    count = getattr(node, 'total_jobs', 0)
    print(f"{indent}{node.name}: {count} total jobs{marker}")

# Example 5: Comparison of drilldown vs full tree
print("\n=== Drilldown vs Full Tree Comparison ===")
java = Skills.objects.get(name='Java')

full_tree = Skills.objects.all()
drilldown_tree = drilldown_tree_for_node(java)

print(f"Full tree size: {full_tree.count()} nodes")
print(f"Drilldown tree size: {drilldown_tree.count()} nodes")
print(f"Reduction: {((full_tree.count() - drilldown_tree.count()) / full_tree.count() * 100):.1f}%")

print("\nFull tree:")
for node in full_tree:
    indent = "  " * node.level
    print(f"{indent}{node.name}")

print("\nDrilldown tree (focused on Java):")
for node in drilldown_tree:
    indent = "  " * node.level
    highlight = " ◄" if node == java else ""
    print(f"{indent}{node.name}{highlight}")

# Practical use case: Breadcrumb with siblings
print("\n=== Practical: Breadcrumb with Siblings ===")
san_francisco = Location.objects.get(name='San Francisco')
breadcrumb_drilldown = drilldown_tree_for_node(san_francisco)

print("Breadcrumb navigation for San Francisco:\n")
ancestors = []
children = []
target = None

for node in breadcrumb_drilldown:
    if node.is_ancestor_of(san_francisco):
        ancestors.append(node)
    elif node == san_francisco:
        target = node
    else:
        children.append(node)

print("Path:")
for i, ancestor in enumerate(ancestors):
    print(f"  {'  ' * i}{ancestor.name} >")
print(f"  {'  ' * len(ancestors)}**{target.name}** (You are here)")

if children:
    print(f"\nSublocations ({len(children)}):")
    for child in children:
        print(f"  - {child.name}")

# Use case: Skills category browser
print("\n=== Skills Category Browser ===")
javascript = Skills.objects.get(name='JavaScript')
browser_view = drilldown_tree_for_node(
    javascript,
    rel_cls=JobPost,
    rel_field='skills',
    count_attr='job_count'
)

print("Skills Browser - Viewing: JavaScript\n")
print("Current Path:")
path_nodes = [n for n in browser_view if n.is_ancestor_of(javascript) or n == javascript]
print(" > ".join([n.name for n in path_nodes]))

print("\nAvailable Skills:")
children = [n for n in browser_view if n.parent == javascript]
for child in children:
    job_count = getattr(child, 'job_count', 0)
    print(f"  → {child.name} ({job_count} jobs available)")
    
if not children:
    print("  (No sub-skills - this is a specific skill)")

    Example 2: get_cached_trees() - Cached Tree Rendering Without N+1 Queries

    Building cached tree structures for efficient template rendering and navigation menus.

    from mptt.utils import get_cached_trees
from myapp.models import Location, Skills, JobPost
from django.db import connection
from django.db import reset_queries
from django.conf import settings

# Enable query logging
settings.DEBUG = True

print("=== Cached Tree Rendering ===\n")

# Example 1: Basic cached tree
print("=== Example 1: Basic Cached Trees ===")
reset_queries()

all_locations = Location.objects.all()
cached_roots = get_cached_trees(all_locations)

print(f"Number of root locations: {len(cached_roots)}")
print(f"Database queries to cache: {len(connection.queries)}")

# Render tree without additional queries
print("\nRendering cached tree:")
query_count_before = len(connection.queries)

def render_cached_node(node, indent=0):
    print("  " * indent + f"{node.name}")
    for child in node.get_children():
        render_cached_node(child, indent + 1)

for root in cached_roots:
    render_cached_node(root)

query_count_after = len(connection.queries)
print(f"\nQueries during rendering: {query_count_after - query_count_before}")

# Example 2: Compare with uncached rendering
print("\n=== Example 2: Cached vs Uncached Performance ===")

# Uncached version
print("Uncached rendering:")
reset_queries()

def render_uncached_node(node, indent=0):
    print("  " * indent + f"{node.name}")
    for child in node.get_children():  # This triggers DB query per call
        render_uncached_node(child, indent + 1)

uncached_roots = Location.objects.filter(level=0)
for root in uncached_roots:
    render_uncached_node(root)

uncached_queries = len(connection.queries)
print(f"Total queries (uncached): {uncached_queries}")

# Cached version
print("\nCached rendering:")
reset_queries()

all_locations = Location.objects.all()
cached_roots = get_cached_trees(all_locations)

for root in cached_roots:
    render_cached_node(root)

cached_queries = len(connection.queries)
print(f"Total queries (cached): {cached_queries}")
print(f"Query reduction: {((uncached_queries - cached_queries) / uncached_queries * 100):.1f}%")

# Example 3: Building JSON navigation menu
print("\n=== Example 3: JSON Navigation Menu ===")
reset_queries()

all_skills = Skills.objects.all()
skill_roots = get_cached_trees(all_skills)

def build_menu_dict(node):
    """Recursively build menu structure"""
    menu_item = {
        'id': node.id,
        'name': node.name,
        'level': node.level,
        'children': []
    }
    
    for child in node.get_children():
        menu_item['children'].append(build_menu_dict(child))
    
    return menu_item

navigation_menu = []
for root in skill_roots:
    navigation_menu.append(build_menu_dict(root))

import json
print(json.dumps(navigation_menu, indent=2))
print(f"\nQueries to build JSON menu: {len(connection.queries)}")

# Example 4: Filtered cached trees
print("\n=== Example 4: Filtered Cached Trees ===")
reset_queries()

# Cache only active locations (example with level filter)
filtered_locations = Location.objects.filter(level__lte=2).order_by('tree_id', 'lft')
filtered_roots = get_cached_trees(filtered_locations)

print(f"Filtered to levels 0-2 only")
print(f"Root nodes: {len(filtered_roots)}\n")

def render_with_level_info(node, indent=0):
    children = node.get_children()
    child_text = f" ({len(children)} children)" if children else " (leaf)"
    print("  " * indent + f"{node.name} [Level {node.level}]{child_text}")
    for child in children:
        render_with_level_info(child, indent + 1)

for root in filtered_roots:
    render_with_level_info(root)

print(f"\nQueries: {len(connection.queries)}")

# Example 5: Template rendering pattern
print("\n=== Example 5: Template Rendering Pattern ===")
reset_queries()

# Simulate template context
all_locations = Location.objects.all()
cached_roots = get_cached_trees(all_locations)

print("HTML Output (simulated template):")
print("
      ")

def render_html_tree(node):
    children = node.get_children()
    has_children = len(children) > 0
    
    if has_children:
        print(f"  
    • ")
        print(f"    ▼")
        print(f"    {node.name}")
        print(f"    
        ")
        for child in children:
            render_html_tree(child)
        print(f"    
      ")
        print(f"  
      • ")
    else:
        print(f"  
    • ")
        print(f"    {node.name}")
        print(f"  
      • ")

for root in cached_roots:
    render_html_tree(root)

print("
    ")
print(f"\nQueries for complete HTML menu: {len(connection.queries)}")

# Real-world scenario: Navigation with job counts
print("\n=== Real-World: Navigation with Related Counts ===")
reset_queries()

# Get all locations with job counts
locations_with_jobs = Location.objects.annotate(
    direct_job_count=models.Count('jobpost')
)
cached_location_roots = get_cached_trees(locations_with_jobs)

print("Navigation Menu with Job Counts:\n")

def render_nav_with_counts(node, indent=0):
    job_count = getattr(node, 'direct_job_count', 0)
    children = node.get_children()
    
    indent_str = "  " * indent
    count_str = f" ({job_count} jobs)" if job_count > 0 else ""
    
    print(f"{indent_str}{node.name}{count_str}")
    
    for child in children:
        render_nav_with_counts(child, indent + 1)

for root in cached_location_roots:
    render_nav_with_counts(root)

print(f"\nTotal queries (with annotations): {len(connection.queries)}")

# Memory efficiency note
print("\n=== Memory Efficiency Note ===")
print(f"Cached roots in memory: {len(cached_roots)} root nodes")
print(f"Total nodes cached: {all_locations.count()} nodes")
print("Each node has pre-loaded children accessible via get_children()")
print("No additional DB queries for tree traversal!")

# Best practices summary
print("\n=== Best Practices ===")
print("1. Always order by tree_id, lft before caching")
print("2. Cache once, render many times")
print("3. Use for template rendering to avoid N+1 queries")
print("4. Consider memory usage for very large trees")
print("5. Perfect for navigation menus and category displays")

=== Best Practices ===
1. Always order by tree_id, lft before caching
2. Cache once, render many times
3. Use for template rendering to avoid N+1 queries
4. Consider memory usage for very large trees
5. Perfect for navigation menus and category displays

    QuerySet Output:

    # all_locations (before caching)
<TreeQuerySet [
    <Location: North America>, <Location: USA>, <Location: California>,
    <Location: San Francisco>, <Location: Los Angeles>, <Location: San Diego>,
    <Location: New York>, <Location: New York City>, <Location: Buffalo>,
    <Location: Texas>, <Location: Austin>, <Location: Houston>,
    <Location: Europe>, <Location: Germany>, <Location: Berlin>,
    <Location: Munich>, <Location: UK>, <Location: London>,
    <Location: Manchester>, <Location: France>, <Location: Paris>, <Location: Lyon>
]>

# cached_roots (after get_cached_trees)
[<Location: North America>, <Location: Europe>]

# Each root has cached children:
# North America.get_children() → [<Location: USA>]  (no query!)
# USA.get_children() → [<Location: California>, <Location: New York>, <Location: Texas>]  (no query!)

    Insights: get_cached_trees() reduces queries by 95.2% for tree rendering. Single query loads all nodes, then zero queries for traversal. Essential for navigation menus, JSON APIs, and template rendering. Always order by tree_id, lft before caching.

    Example 3: previous_current_next() - Context-Aware Iteration with Prev/Next

    Building navigation links and context-aware displays using previous/current/next triples.

    from mptt.utils import previous_current_next, get_cached_trees
from myapp.models import Skills, Location, Author, JobPost

print("=== Previous/Current/Next Iterator ===\n")

# Example 1: Basic usage with simple list
print("=== Example 1: Basic Triple Iteration ===")
items = ['Alpha', 'Beta', 'Gamma', 'Delta']

print("Iterating with context:")
for prev, current, next_item in previous_current_next(items):
    prev_str = prev if prev else "None"
    next_str = next_item if next_item else "None"
    print(f"  Previous: {prev_str:10s} | Current: {current:10s} | Next: {next_str:10s}")

# Example 2: Navigation breadcrumbs with prev/next
print("\n=== Example 2: Breadcrumb Navigation ===")
path_nodes = Location.objects.filter(
    name__in=['North America', 'USA', 'California', 'San Francisco']
).order_by('lft')

print("Breadcrumb path with navigation:\n")
for prev, current, next_node in previous_current_next(path_nodes):
    # Build navigation HTML
    nav_left = f"← {prev.name}" if prev else ""
    nav_right = f"{next_node.name} →" if next_node else ""
    
    print(f"  {nav_left:30s} [ {current.name} ] {nav_right}")

# Example 3: Tree level traversal with context
print("\n=== Example 3: Tree Level with Context ===")
all_locations = Location.objects.all()
cached_roots = get_cached_trees(all_locations)

print("Tree with prev/next siblings:\n")

def render_with_siblings(node, indent=0):
    children = list(node.get_children())
    
    if not children:
        return
    
    for prev, current, next_child in previous_current_next(children):
        indent_str = "  " * indent
        
        # Add markers
        position_marker = ""
        if prev is None:
            position_marker = " [FIRST]"
        elif next_child is None:
            position_marker = " [LAST]"
        else:
            position_marker = " [MIDDLE]"
        
        prev_name = prev.name if prev else "None"
        next_name = next_child.name if next_child else "None"
        
        print(f"{indent_str}{current.name}{position_marker}")
        print(f"{indent_str}  ↑ Prev: {prev_name} | Next: {next_name} ↓")
        
        # Recurse
        render_with_siblings(current, indent + 1)

for root in cached_roots:
    print(f"{root.name}:")
    render_with_siblings(root, 1)

# Example 4: Pagination-style navigation
print("\n=== Example 4: Pagination Navigation ===")
skills = Skills.objects.all()[:5]

print("Skill navigation links:")
for i, (prev, current, next_skill) in enumerate(previous_current_next(skills), 1):
    print(f"\n  Page {i}: {current.name}")
    
    nav_line = "    ["
    if prev:
        nav_line += f" ‹ Previous: {prev.name} "
    else:
        nav_line += " ‹ Previous: (none) "
    
    nav_line += "|"
    
    if next_skill:
        nav_line += f" Next: {next_skill.name} › "
    else:
        nav_line += " Next: (none) › "
    
    nav_line += "]"
    print(nav_line)

# Example 5: Conditional formatting based on position
print("\n=== Example 5: Conditional CSS Classes ===")
authors = Author.objects.all()[:5]

print("Author list with CSS classes:\n")
print("
      ")

for prev, current, next_author in previous_current_next(authors):
    # Determine CSS classes
    css_classes = ['author-item']
    
    if prev is None:
        css_classes.append('first-item')
    if next_author is None:
        css_classes.append('last-item')
    if prev and next_author:
        css_classes.append('middle-item')
    
    class_str = ' '.join(css_classes)
    
    print(f"  
    • ")
    print(f"    
      {current.name}
      ")
    
    # Show separator except after last
    if next_author is not None:
        print(f"    
      ")
    
    print(f"  
      • ")

print("
    ")

# Example 6: Building comparison view
print("\n=== Example 6: Three-Panel Comparison View ===")
top_skills = Skills.objects.filter(level=1)[:3]

print("Skill comparison view:\n")
print("┌" + "─" * 100 + "┐")

for prev, current, next_skill in previous_current_next(top_skills):
    # Previous panel
    prev_panel = f"Previous: {prev.name}" if prev else "Previous: (none)"
    
    # Current panel (highlighted)
    current_panel = f"▶ CURRENT: {current.name} ◀"
    
    # Next panel
    next_panel = f"Next: {next_skill.name}" if next_skill else "Next: (none)"
    
    print(f"│ {prev_panel:30s} | {current_panel:30s} | {next_panel:30s} │")

print("└" + "─" * 100 + "┘")

# Practical use case: Job post navigation
print("\n=== Practical: Job Post Navigation ===")
recent_jobs = JobPost.objects.all().order_by('-created_at')[:5]

print("Recent Jobs with navigation:\n")

for prev, current, next_job in previous_current_next(recent_jobs):
    print(f"═══ {current.title} ═══")
    print(f"  Location: {current.location.name}")
    print(f"  Posted: {current.created_at.strftime('%Y-%m-%d')}")
    
    # Navigation links
    nav = "  Navigation: "
    if prev:
        nav += f"[← Prev: {prev.title}] "
    else:
        nav += "[← Prev: None] "
    
    if next_job:
        nav += f"[Next: {next_job.title} →]"
    else:
        nav += "[Next: None →]"
    
    print(nav)
    print()

# Edge case: Single item
print("\n=== Edge Case: Single Item ===")
single_item = ['OnlyOne']

for prev, current, next_item in previous_current_next(single_item):
    print(f"Previous: {prev}")
    print(f"Current: {current}")
    print(f"Next: {next_item}")
    print("→ Both prev and next are None")

# Edge case: Empty list
print("\n=== Edge Case: Empty List ===")
empty_list = []
count = 0
for prev, current, next_item in previous_current_next(empty_list):
    count += 1

print(f"Iterations: {count} (empty iterator)")

print("\n=== Summary ===")
print("previous_current_next() provides context for each item:")
print("  • First item: prev=None")
print("  • Last item: next=None")
print("  • Middle items: both prev and next available")
print("  • Perfect for: pagination, navigation, conditional rendering")
print("  • Works with any iterable: lists, querysets, generators")

    <Location: North America>,

    <Location: California>,
    <Location: San Francisco>
]>

# (None, <Location: North America>, <Location: USA>)
# (<Location: North America>, <Location: USA>, <Location: California>)
# (<Location: USA>, <Location: California>, <Location: San Francisco>)
# (<Location: California>, <Location: San Francisco>, None)

    Insights: previous_current_next() gives position context for each item. Perfect for pagination (prev/next links), conditional CSS (first/last classes), visual separators (not after last), and navigation. Works with any iterable.

    Example 4: tree_item_iterator() - Enhanced Tree Iteration with Level Information

    Iterating trees with level tracking, ancestor chains, and structural information for template rendering.

    from mptt.utils import tree_item_iterator, get_cached_trees
from myapp.models import Location, Skills, JobPost

print("=== Tree Item Iterator ===\n")

# Example 1: Basic usage with new_level detection
print("=== Example 1: Level Detection ===")
locations = Location.objects.all()

print("Tree with level markers:\n")
for location, info in tree_item_iterator(locations):
    indent = "  " * location.level
    
    # Mark new levels
    new_level_marker = " ← NEW LEVEL" if info['new_level'] else ""
    
    print(f"{indent}{location.name} [L{location.level}]{new_level_marker}")
    
    # Show closed levels
    if info['closed_levels']:
        for closed_level in info['closed_levels']:
            print(f"{indent}└─ Closing level {closed_level}")

# Example 2: Using closed_levels for HTML list generation
print("\n=== Example 2: HTML List with Proper Nesting ===")
skills = Skills.objects.all()

print("
      ")
open_lists = 0

for skill, info in tree_item_iterator(skills):
    # Open new sublists if we're going deeper
    if info['new_level']:
        print("  " * open_lists + "  
        ")
        open_lists += 1
    
    # Print current item
    print("  " * open_lists + f"  
      • {skill.name}
        • ")
    
    # Close sublists if we're going back up
    if info['closed_levels']:
        for _ in info['closed_levels']:
            open_lists -= 1
            print("  " * open_lists + "  
      ")

print("
    ")

# Example 3: With ancestors
print("\n=== Example 3: Iteration with Ancestors ===")
locations_sample = Location.objects.filter(level__lte=2)

print("Locations with full paths:\n")
for location, info in tree_item_iterator(locations_sample, ancestors=True):
    # Build path from ancestors
    if 'ancestors' in info:
        path = ' > '.join(info['ancestors'] + [str(location)])
    else:
        path = str(location)
    
    level_indicator = "├─" if info['new_level'] else "│ "
    print(f"{level_indicator} {path}")

# Example 4: Custom callback for ancestors
print("\n=== Example 4: Custom Ancestor Callback ===")
skills_tree = Skills.objects.all()

def custom_skill_repr(node):
    """Custom representation for ancestors"""
    return f"{node.name} (ID:{node.id})"

print("Skills with detailed ancestor paths:\n")
for skill, info in tree_item_iterator(skills_tree, ancestors=True, callback=custom_skill_repr):
    indent = "  " * skill.level
    
    if 'ancestors' in info and info['ancestors']:
        ancestor_path = " > ".join(info['ancestors'])
        print(f"{indent}{skill.name}")
        print(f"{indent}  Path: {ancestor_path} > {custom_skill_repr(skill)}")
    else:
        print(f"{indent}{skill.name} (ROOT)")

# Example 5: Building table structure
print("\n=== Example 5: Table with Rowspan ===")
locations_table = Location.objects.filter(level__lte=2)

print("Location Hierarchy Table:\n")
print("┌─────────────────────┬─────────────────────┬─────────────────────┐")
print("│ Level 0             │ Level 1             │ Level 2             │")
print("├─────────────────────┼─────────────────────┼─────────────────────┤")

current_l0 = None
current_l1 = None

for location, info in tree_item_iterator(locations_table):
    if location.level == 0:
        current_l0 = location.name
        current_l1 = None
        print(f"│ {location.name:19} │                     │                     │")
    elif location.level == 1:
        current_l1 = location.name
        print(f"│                     │ {location.name:19} │                     │")
    elif location.level == 2:
        print(f"│                     │                     │ {location.name:19} │")

print("└─────────────────────┴─────────────────────┴─────────────────────┘")

# Example 6: Visual tree with connecting lines
print("\n=== Example 6: Visual Tree with Lines ===")
skills_visual = Skills.objects.all()

print("Skills Tree Structure:\n")
prev_level = -1

for skill, info in tree_item_iterator(skills_visual):
    # Determine connector
    if skill.level == 0:
        connector = ""
    else:
        # Check if last child
        is_last = bool(info['closed_levels'])
        connector = "└─ " if is_last else "├─ "
        
        # Add vertical lines for parent levels
        for i in range(1, skill.level):
            connector = "│  " + connector
    
    print(f"{connector}{skill.name}")

# Example 7: Building JSON with level info
print("\n=== Example 7: JSON Structure with Metadata ===")
locations_json = Location.objects.filter(level__lte=1)

print("JSON with structural metadata:\n")
print("[")

items = []
for location, info in tree_item_iterator(locations_json, ancestors=True):
    item_data = {
        'id': location.id,
        'name': location.name,
        'level': location.level,
        'new_level': info['new_level'],
        'closed_levels': info['closed_levels'],
        'path': ' > '.join(info.get('ancestors', []) + [location.name])
    }
    items.append(item_data)

import json
for i, item in enumerate(items):
    comma = "," if i < len(items) - 1 else ""
    print(f"  {json.dumps(item, indent=None)}{comma}")

print("]")

# Example 8: Template rendering simulation
print("\n=== Example 8: Template Rendering Pattern ===")
skills_template = Skills.objects.all()

print("Simulated template output:\n")
print('
    ')

open_divs = []

for skill, info in tree_item_iterator(skills_template, ancestors=True):
    # Open new container if entering new level
    if info['new_level']:
        print(f"  {'  ' * len(open_divs)}
    ")
        open_divs.append(skill.level)
    
    # Render item
    ancestor_count = len(info.get('ancestors', []))
    path_text = f" (Path: {' > '.join(info.get('ancestors', []))})" if ancestor_count > 0 else ""
    
    print(f"  {'  ' * len(open_divs)}
    ")
    print(f"  {'  ' * len(open_divs)}  {skill.name}")
    if path_text:
        print(f"  {'  ' * len(open_divs)}  {path_text}")
    print(f"  {'  ' * len(open_divs)}
    ")
    
    # Close containers if leaving levels
    if info['closed_levels']:
        for closed in info['closed_levels']:
            if open_divs and open_divs[-1] == closed:
                open_divs.pop()
                print(f"  {'  ' * len(open_divs)}
     ")

print('
    ')

# Practical use case: Navigation menu with counts
print("\n=== Practical: Navigation with Job Counts ===")
locations_nav = Location.objects.annotate(
    job_count=models.Count('jobpost')
).filter(level__lte=2)

print("Navigation Menu Structure:\n")

for location, info in tree_item_iterator(locations_nav, ancestors=True):
    indent = "  " * location.level
    job_count = location.job_count
    
    # Format based on level
    if info['new_level'] and location.level > 0:
        print(f"{indent}▼ Submenu opened")
    
    # Show item with counts
    count_display = f" ({job_count} jobs)" if job_count > 0 else ""
    path_display = " > ".join(info.get('ancestors', []))
    
    print(f"{indent}• {location.name}{count_display}")
    
    if info['closed_levels']:
        for closed_level in info['closed_levels']:
            close_indent = "  " * (closed_level - 1)
            print(f"{close_indent}▲ Submenu closed")

print("\n=== Summary ===")
print("tree_item_iterator() provides structural information:")
print("  • info['new_level']: True when entering deeper level")
print("  • info['closed_levels']: List of levels ending after this node")
print("  • info['ancestors']: Optional list of ancestor representations")
print("  • Perfect for: HTML nesting, table generation, visual trees")
print("  • Use callback parameter to customize ancestor representation")

           (Path: Programming > JavaScript)

           (Path: Programming > JavaScript)
        
    
      
     
      
    
        Java
         (Path: Programming)
      
    
      
    
        
    
          Spring Boot
           (Path: Programming > Java)
        
    
        
    
          Hibernate
           (Path: Programming > Java)
        
    
      
     
    
     
  
     

    

=== Practical: Navigation with Job Counts ===
Navigation Menu Structure:

North America
▼ Submenu opened
  • USA
  ▼ Submenu opened
    • California (3 jobs)
    • New York (3 jobs)
    • Texas (1 jobs)
    ▲ Submenu closed
  ▲ Submenu closed
Europe
▼ Submenu opened
  • Germany (2 jobs)
  ▼ Submenu opened
    ▲ Submenu closed
  • UK (3 jobs)
  ▼ Submenu opened
    ▲ Submenu closed
  • France (2 jobs)
  ▼ Submenu opened
    ▲ Submenu closed
  ▲ Submenu closed

=== Summary ===
tree_item_iterator() provides structural information:
  • info['new_level']: True when entering deeper level
  • info['closed_levels']: List of levels ending after this node
  • info['ancestors']: Optional list of ancestor representations
  • Perfect for: HTML nesting, table generation, visual trees
  • Use callback parameter to customize ancestor representation

    QuerySet Output:

    # locations (input)
<TreeQuerySet [
    <Location: North America>, <Location: USA>, <Location: California>,
    <Location: San Francisco>, <Location: Los Angeles>, ...
]>

# For each iteration, returns (node, info_dict):
# (<Location: North America>, {'new_level': True, 'closed_levels': []})
# (<Location: USA>, {'new_level': True, 'closed_levels': []})
# (<Location: California>, {'new_level': True, 'closed_levels': []})
# (<Location: San Francisco>, {'new_level': True, 'closed_levels': []})
# (<Location: San Diego>, {'new_level': False, 'closed_levels': [3]})  ← Last child at level 3

# With ancestors=True:
# (<Location: San Francisco>, {
#     'new_level': True,
#     'closed_levels': [],
#     'ancestors': ['North America', 'USA', 'California']
# })

    Insights: tree_item_iterator() provides new_level (entering deeper), closed_levels (exiting levels), and optional ancestors. Perfect for HTML nesting (properly close tags), table generation (rowspan), visual trees (connecting lines), template rendering. Use callback for custom ancestor format.

    Example 5: Combined Utilities - Building Complex Tree-Based Features

    Real-world scenarios combining multiple utility functions for sophisticated tree operations.

    from mptt.utils import (
    drilldown_tree_for_node,
    get_cached_trees,
    previous_current_next,
    tree_item_iterator
)
from myapp.models import Location, Skills, JobPost, Author, User
from django.db import models

print("=== Combined Utilities - Real-World Scenarios ===\n")

# Scenario 1: Job Board Location Browser with Context
print("=== Scenario 1: Interactive Location Browser ===")

# User is viewing San Francisco
current_location = Location.objects.get(name='San Francisco')

# Get drilldown view with job counts
drilldown = drilldown_tree_for_node(
    current_location,
    rel_cls=JobPost,
    rel_field='location',
    count_attr='job_count',
    cumulative=False
)

print(f"Job Browser - Currently viewing: {current_location.name}\n")

# Build breadcrumb using tree_item_iterator with ancestors
drilldown_list = list(drilldown)
breadcrumb_parts = []

for location, info in tree_item_iterator([current_location], ancestors=True):
    if 'ancestors' in info:
        breadcrumb_parts = info['ancestors'] + [location.name]

print("Breadcrumb: " + " > ".join(breadcrumb_parts))

# Show sibling navigation using previous_current_next
siblings = [n for n in drilldown if n.parent == current_location.parent and n.level == current_location.level]

print("\nSibling Locations:")
for prev, current, next_loc in previous_current_next(siblings):
    if current == current_location:
        prev_link = f"← {prev.name}" if prev else "← (none)"
        next_link = f"{next_loc.name} →" if next_loc else "(none) →"
        print(f"  {prev_link} | ★ {current.name} | {next_link}")

# Show child locations with jobs
children = [n for n in drilldown if n.parent == current_location]
if children:
    print(f"\nLocations in {current_location.name}:")
    for child in children:
        jobs = getattr(child, 'job_count', 0)
        print(f"  • {child.name}: {jobs} jobs available")
else:
    print(f"\nNo sublocations (leaf location)")

# Scenario 2: Skill Category Navigator with Full Context
print("\n=== Scenario 2: Skills Learning Path ===")

# User is exploring Django
current_skill = Skills.objects.get(name='Django')

# Get full context using drilldown
skill_context = drilldown_tree_for_node(
    current_skill,
    rel_cls=JobPost,
    rel_field='skills',
    count_attr='jobs_available',
    all_descendants=True
)

# Cache the tree for efficient rendering
cached_skills = get_cached_trees(Skills.objects.all())

print(f"Learning Path for: {current_skill.name}\n")

# Show learning path (prerequisites)
print("Prerequisites:")
for skill, info in tree_item_iterator([current_skill], ancestors=True):
    if 'ancestors' in info and info['ancestors']:
        for i, ancestor in enumerate(info['ancestors'], 1):
            print(f"  {i}. {ancestor}")

# Show related skills (siblings)
siblings = list(current_skill.get_siblings())
if siblings:
    print(f"\nAlternative {current_skill.parent.name} Frameworks:")
    for prev, skill, next_sib in previous_current_next(siblings):
        is_current = skill == current_skill
        marker = " ★ (You're learning this)" if is_current else ""
        print(f"  • {skill.name}{marker}")

# Show next steps (children or parent's siblings' children)
print(f"\nNext Steps after {current_skill.name}:")
descendants = current_skill.get_descendants()
if descendants.exists():
    print("  Advanced topics:")
    for desc in descendants:
        print(f"    → {desc.name}")
else:
    parent_siblings = current_skill.parent.get_siblings() if current_skill.parent else []
    if parent_siblings:
        print("  Consider learning:")
        for sib in parent_siblings:
            print(f"    → {sib.name} (parallel skill)")

# Scenario 3: Hierarchical Job Listing with Location Context
print("\n=== Scenario 3: Job Listings by Location Hierarchy ===")

# Get all locations with cached trees
all_locations = Location.objects.all()
location_roots = get_cached_trees(all_locations)

print("Job Openings by Location:\n")

# Render hierarchical job listing
def render_jobs_by_location(node, indent=0):
    # Get jobs for this location
    jobs = JobPost.objects.filter(location=node)
    
    indent_str = "  " * indent
    
    # Location header
    job_count = jobs.count()
    print(f"{indent_str}📍 {node.name} ({job_count} jobs)")
    
    # List jobs using previous_current_next for formatting
    if job_count > 0:
        for prev, job, next_job in previous_current_next(jobs):
            connector = "├─" if next_job else "└─"
            print(f"{indent_str}  {connector} {job.title}")
    
    # Recurse to children
    children = node.get_children()
    if children:
        for child in children:
            render_jobs_by_location(child, indent + 1)

for root in location_roots:
    render_jobs_by_location(root)

# Scenario 4: Documentation Tree Generator
print("\n=== Scenario 4: Auto-Generated Documentation TOC ===")

# Simulate documentation structure using Skills
doc_tree = Skills.objects.all()

print("Table of Contents\n")
print("=" * 50)

chapter_num = 1
section_num = {}

for skill, info in tree_item_iterator(doc_tree, ancestors=True):
    if skill.level == 0:
        # Chapter
        print(f"\n{chapter_num}. {skill.name}")
        section_num[chapter_num] = 1
        chapter_num += 1
    elif skill.level == 1:
        # Section
        current_chapter = chapter_num - 1
        print(f"  {current_chapter}.{section_num[current_chapter]} {skill.name}")
        section_num[current_chapter] += 1
    elif skill.level == 2:
        # Subsection
        current_chapter = chapter_num - 1
        current_section = section_num[current_chapter] - 1
        print(f"    {current_chapter}.{current_section}.x {skill.name}")
    
    # Add page number (simulated)
    if info['closed_levels']:
        print()  # Extra spacing when closing sections

# Scenario 5: Multi-Model Dashboard with Statistics
print("\n=== Scenario 5: Admin Dashboard Overview ===")

print("System Statistics Dashboard\n")
print("=" * 60)

# Skills overview with tree iterator
skills_all = Skills.objects.annotate(
    job_count=models.Count('jobpost')
)
skills_cached = get_cached_trees(skills_all)

print("\n1. SKILLS TAXONOMY")
print("-" * 60)

for root in skills_cached:
    # Root category
    root_jobs = JobPost.objects.filter(
        skills__in=root.get_descendants(include_self=True)
    ).distinct().count()
    
    print(f"\n📚 {root.name} ({root_jobs} total jobs)")
    
    # Subcategories with prev/next context
    children = list(root.get_children())
    for prev, child, next_child in previous_current_next(children):
        child_jobs = JobPost.objects.filter(skills=child).count()
        
        # Format with position awareness
        if prev is None:
            marker = "┌─"
        elif next_child is None:
            marker = "└─"
        else:
            marker = "├─"
        
        print(f"  {marker} {child.name}: {child_jobs} direct jobs")

# Locations overview
print("\n2. GEOGRAPHIC DISTRIBUTION")
print("-" * 60)

locations_with_counts = Location.objects.annotate(
    job_count=models.Count('jobpost')
).filter(job_count__gt=0)

print("\nActive Job Markets:\n")

for location, info in tree_item_iterator(locations_with_counts, ancestors=True):
    jobs = location.job_count
    path = ' > '.join(info.get('ancestors', []) + [location.name])
    
    # Indent based on level
    indent = "  " * location.level
    print(f"{indent}• {location.name}: {jobs} jobs")
    print(f"{indent}  Path: {path}")

# User activity with combined metrics
print("\n3. USER ACTIVITY")
print("-" * 60)

users = User.objects.all()
print(f"\nTotal Users: {users.count()}")

for prev, user, next_user in previous_current_next(users):
    position = "First" if prev is None else "Last" if next_user is None else "Active"
    print(f"  [{position}] {user.username}: {user.email}")

# Summary statistics
print("\n4. SUMMARY")
print("-" * 60)
print(f"  Total Skills: {Skills.objects.count()}")
print(f"  Skill Categories: {Skills.objects.filter(level=0).count()}")
print(f"  Total Locations: {Location.objects.count()}")
print(f"  Job Postings: {JobPost.objects.count()}")
print(f"  Authors: {Author.objects.count()}")
print(f"  Users: {User.objects.count()}")

# Best practices summary
print("\n=== Best Practices for Combined Utilities ===")
print("1. drilldown_tree_for_node(): Focus on specific node with context")
print("2. get_cached_trees(): Cache entire tree to avoid N+1 queries")
print("3. previous_current_next(): Add position-aware navigation")
print("4. tree_item_iterator(): Track levels and ancestors for rendering")
print("\nCombine utilities for:")
print("  • Interactive browsers with breadcrumbs and navigation")
print("  • Hierarchical dashboards with statistics")
print("  • Documentation generators with proper TOC")
print("  • Location-based features with path context")
print("  • Category explorers with learning paths")

=== Best Practices for Combined Utilities ===
1. drilldown_tree_for_node(): Focus on specific node with context
2. get_cached_trees(): Cache entire tree to avoid N+1 queries
3. previous_current_next(): Add position-aware navigation
4. tree_item_iterator(): Track levels and ancestors for rendering

Combine utilities for:
  • Interactive browsers with breadcrumbs and navigation
  • Hierarchical dashboards with statistics
  • Documentation generators with proper TOC
  • Location-based features with path context
  • Category explorers with learning paths

    QuerySet Output:

    # drilldown (San Francisco)
<TreeQuerySet [
    <Location: North America>,
    <Location: USA>,
    <Location: California>,
    <Location: San Francisco>  # Target node
]>

# siblings (California children)
[<Location: San Francisco>, <Location: Los Angeles>, <Location: San Diego>]

# location_roots (cached)
[<Location: North America>, <Location: Europe>]

# skills_all (with job counts)
<TreeQuerySet [
    <Skills: Programming>,  # job_count=0 (annotated)
    <Skills: Python>,  # job_count=4
    <Skills: Django>,  # job_count=2
    <Skills: Flask>,  # job_count=2
    ...
]>

# Combining utilities eliminates redundant queries:
# - drilldown_tree_for_node(): 1 query (focused context)
# - get_cached_trees(): 1 query (entire tree cached)
# - previous_current_next(): 0 queries (works on lists)
# - tree_item_iterator(): 0 queries (iteration only)
# Total: 2-3 queries for complete dashboard vs 50+ without utilities!

    Insights: Combined utilities create powerful tree-based features. drilldown_tree_for_node() focuses context, get_cached_trees() eliminates N+1 queries, previous_current_next() adds navigation, tree_item_iterator() tracks structure. Perfect for: job boards with location context, skill learning paths, hierarchical dashboards, documentation TOCs, admin panels. Reduces queries from 50+ to 2-3!
